201404	24	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201404	25	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Without objection.	92	9
201404	26	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	I would like to start off our session this morning with a few remarks on the objectives and timetable for our work on monetary policy normalization.	92	9
201404	27	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Before doing so, though, I want to give special thanks to the staff for all their hard work on these complicated issues and for the excellent set of memos that they prepared for this meeting.	92	9
201404	28	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Let me begin by saying I am completely convinced that we have the tools to adjust the stance of policy as needed to meet our macroeconomic objectives.	92	9
201404	29	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	So this discussion is about how to deploy our mix of tools to attain these objectives most effectively in a way that balances other considerations appropriately.	92	9
201404	30	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	As the briefing materials make clear, however, there is quite a mix of subtle and intertwined issues to take into account, involving market functioning, the scope of our activities in the nonbank sector, communications, financial stability, and possible implications of our current choices for our longer-run operating procedure.	92	9
201404	31	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	I don’t want to get into the substance of these issues at this point.	92	9
201404	32	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	I just want to make a few overarching comments that may serve to frame our discussion.	92	9
201404	33	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	If the recovery proceeds broadly as we expect, we will likely begin to raise interest rates sometime next year.	92	9
201404	34	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	I believe it is important that we communicate our normalization plans to the public well before that time.	92	9
201404	35	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	I would see the press conference after the September meeting as potentially providing a good opportunity to lay out for the public some of our thinking on these matters.	92	9
201404	36	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	If you agree with this timetable, we will need to make substantial progress in nailing down our approach over the course of this meeting and, then, the June and July meetings.	92	9
201404	37	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	There are difficult issues here, which we need to work through collectively, before we can be confident that we are ready to manage the normalization process and convey that confidence to the public.	92	9
201404	38	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	So I think a concentrated effort will surely be required to make the necessary progress by September.	92	9
201404	39	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Of course—and fortunately—we are not starting from scratch.	92	9
201404	40	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Our deliberations will build on our earlier discussions of normalization and draw on the results from the ongoing testing of our tools.	92	9
201404	41	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	One lesson from our earlier efforts at spelling out our exit strategy, which is a topic we discussed at length in our meeting just a year ago, is that what may seem perfectly sensible ex ante may end up seeming much less attractive as conditions change in unforeseen ways.	92	9
201404	42	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	I think we need to accept the reality that we cannot know exactly what kind of market conditions and considerations we will face when the time comes to begin raising rates.	92	9
201404	43	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	And we cannot know with precision how well any particular strategy will work.	92	9
201404	44	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	So, while I don’t want to prejudge any decisions on specific issues, I believe it is important that we create a framework in which we can deploy our mix of tools relatively flexibly to deal with contingencies that may arise.	92	9
201404	45	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	But it is equally important that we agree on a framework that we can explain simply and clearly, so as to convincingly convey our confidence that we can adjust the stance of policy as appropriate to promote our macroeconomic objectives.	92	9
201404	46	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	I think we should also provide clarity, to the extent possible, about the mechanics of our approach in order to ease the transition for market participants, particularly in those markets in which we may be acting in new ways.	92	9
201404	47	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	And I think our success will depend in part on our communication strategy.	92	9
201404	48	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	I want to end by encouraging everyone to be open to the range of possibilities before us and to keep in mind our overarching goals.	92	9
201404	49	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Despite the timetable I indicated, there is no need to reach firm conclusions at this meeting.	92	9
201404	50	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	My hope is that over the course of today’s discussion we can begin to locate, and then refine, our sense of common ground—that we can share frankly our individual perspectives and reservations, and, more pragmatically, perhaps, we can rule out at least some alternatives in order to narrow the field of our future decisionmaking.	92	9
201404	51	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	We have asked you to weigh in on a number of different questions to provide some preliminary feel for where common ground may lie.	92	9
201404	52	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	But at this stage, your answers to some of the questions may be that you just don’t know and are open to different possibilities, and that is a perfectly fine answer.	92	9

201404	59	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201404	60	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	I will be referring to the handout titled “Material for Briefing on the Monetary Policy Normalization.”	92	9
201404	61	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	In our briefing today, we will review some key points from the memos on normalization that you received over the intermeeting period.	92	9
201404	62	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The first exhibit summarizes information from the memo that outlined near-term approaches for conducting policy with a large balance sheet.	92	9
201404	63	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	As noted in the top-left panel, the Committee has a number of tools to use to raise rates.	92	9
201404	64	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Increasing interest on excess reserves will likely, by itself, raise short- term rates, but these rates could potentially not increase one-for-one and could vary relative to IOER rate over time.	92	9
201404	65	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The Committee has at its disposal several tools that could be used in various combinations to improve control over the level of short-term rates, including overnight repurchase agreements (which I’ll refer to as ON RRPs), term RRPs, and term deposits.	92	9
201404	66	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	As noted to the right, the memo considers five options for implementing normalization.	92	9
201404	67	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Of course, the Committee is not constrained to choose a single option; it could choose a mix of options or adapt its policy approach over time, observing the effects of its policies and making adjustments along the way.	92	9
201404	68	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The key features of the five options presented in the memo are summarized in the middle panel.	92	9
201404	69	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The first three options would combine IOER with a full-allotment ON RRP facility and would not use term draining tools.	92	9
201404	70	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The ON RRP facility would likely help to set a floor under overnight rates, as investors with access to the facility rate would not have an incentive to lend to any counterparty below this rate.	92	9
201404	71	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	I should note at the outset that the Committee might want to impose limits on the allotment of its ON RRP facility in order to support financial stability; such limits could be used in any of the options.	92	9
201404	72	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	In option 1, the ON RRP rate is set equal to the IOER rate, and these rates would be the center of policy communication.	92	9
201404	73	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The next two options are similar to option 1, but with the ON RRP rate set below the IOER rate.	92	9
201404	74	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	In option 2, the spread would be small, with the Committee targeting an administered rate or possibly an alternative overnight market rate, such as the ON GC repo rate.	92	9
201404	75	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	In option 3, the spread between the ON RRP rate and the IOER rate would be larger, and the ON RRP rate would be adjusted to move the federal funds rate to the desired target rate or range set by the Committee.	92	9
201404	76	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The spread between the ON RRP rate and the IOER rate is larger in option 3 than in option 2 in order to maintain incentives for the federal funds trading that we currently see.	92	9
201404	77	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Option 4 also uses IOER but introduces term draining tools along with an ON RRP facility.	92	9
201404	78	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Here the ON RRP rate is set well below the IOER rate, to support trading in the funds market.	92	9
201404	79	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Term draining operations would be used as necessary to hit the target funds rate or range.	92	9
201404	80	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Option 5 is the approach envisioned by the Committee a few years ago, prior to the introduction of the ON RRP exercise.	92	9
201404	81	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Here IOER would be supplemented only with term draining tools to tighten the relationship between the IOER rate and market rates.	92	9
201404	82	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	In options 4 and 5, the quantity of reserves needed to be drained would be uncertain and would depend on the level of the federal funds rate target chosen and the desired spread between the IOER rate and federal funds rate.	92	9
201404	83	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	It is possible that policymakers would judge the relationship between the IOER rate and the federal funds rate to be sufficiently stable after relatively little draining of reserves.	92	9
201404	84	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Alternatively, if a very large amount of reserves needed to be drained, the Federal Reserve might have to build a large book of term deposits and term RRPs.	92	9
201404	85	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The bottom panel lists six key policy issues that you may want to consider as you evaluate these alternative approaches.	92	9
201404	86	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	First, you may want to evaluate how the options differ in terms of their control of short-term interest rates.	92	9
201404	87	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	By increasing the IOER rate, all options can likely move market rates higher, but the degree of control is uncertain.	92	9
201404	88	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The ON RRP exercise suggests that such a facility is likely to help set a firmer floor on market rates.	92	9
201404	89	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Option 1, with the ON RRP rate set to the IOER rate, would likely result in the most control, because other short-term money market rates would probably trade at or slightly above these two administered rates.	92	9
201404	90	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The other options, in which the ON RRP rate is set below the IOER rate, may see market rates trade between the two administered rates.	92	9
201404	91	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Of course, use of the term tools, as under options 4 or 5, could help to improve control as well, though the extent of the required operations is uncertain.	92	9
201404	92	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Second, you may want to evaluate how efficient the options are in conducting monetary policy.	92	9
201404	93	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	It is difficult to determine each option’s full range of effects on financial markets and financial intermediation.	92	9
201404	94	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	That said, if you prefer to have interest rates on similar assets set at similar levels, then you may prefer a relatively narrow spread between the IOER rate and other overnight administered and market rates, as in options 1 or 2.	92	9
201404	95	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	You may also want to take account of the effects of the different options on the level of reserve balances and the efficiency of financial intermediation.	92	9
201404	96	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Third, you will need to decide whether you want to have an active federal funds market, so you can continue to target the federal funds rate.	92	9
201404	97	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	In options that include no spread or a fairly narrow spread between the IOER and ON RRP rates, such as options 1 and 2, trading in the federal funds market would likely decline to a level that may lead the federal funds effective rate to become less tightly connected to other money market rates.	92	9
201404	98	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Josh will talk about issues related to the functioning of the funds market and possible adjustments that the Committee could make.	92	9
201404	99	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Fourth, you will need to consider the potential financial-stability implications of these options and particularly of the introduction of a full-allotment ON RRP facility.	92	9
201404	100	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	As Antoine and Fabio will discuss in a few minutes, there are potential financial- stability benefits and costs to having such a facility, and there are steps that could be taken to mitigate some of the costs.	92	9
201404	101	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Fifth, you will probably want to assess the possible implications of extending the Fed’s footprint in the nonbank financial sector.	92	9
201404	102	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	In particular, ON and term RRPs would increase the Federal Reserve’s direct interaction with nonbank counterparties, and possibly substantially so.	92	9
201404	103	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	There are benefits to interacting with nonbanks, such as increasing competition among money market participants for the Federal Reserve’s assets, which can enhance the Fed’s ability to influence the level of short-term rates.	92	9
201404	104	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	But there are costs that must also be weighed, including the “optics” of relying heavily on GSEs and money funds to conduct policy.	92	9
201404	105	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	In practice, the extent of the Federal Reserve’s interaction with such counterparties would be influenced by the relative setting of the administered rates and any quantity limits associated with the operations.	92	9
201404	106	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Sixth, you should be aware of the potential consequences—both financial and political—associated with how these options would affect the Federal Reserve’s interest expense and, hence, its remittances to the Treasury.	92	9
201404	107	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Such effects would depend on take-up and the effect on market rates.	92	9
201404	108	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	It seems likely that term tools, with their relatively high rates, would be more costly than overnight tools, but of course it would depend on the volume of reserves drained.	92	9
201404	109	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	An option in which the ON RRP rate is set near the IOER rate would likely be the least costly option, because market rates would likely be closest to the IOER rate in that case.	92	9
201404	110	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Finally, I would note that one of the memos laid out options for additional testing of your tools.	92	9
201404	111	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The specific plan for near-term testing of term deposits includes eight consecutive, weekly, seven-day term deposit operations starting in mid-May.	92	9
201404	112	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The first four operations envisioned would incrementally raise the maximum individual award amount from the current $1.25 billion to $10 billion, with offering rates maintained at 1 basis point above the IOER rate.	92	9
201404	113	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	The subsequent four operations would gradually increase the rate paid on term deposits to a maximum of 5 basis points above the IOER rate.	92	9
201404	114	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	We would be interested in your views on this and other testing that you might find helpful as you consider these issues.	92	9
201404	115	2014-04-30	meeting	IHRIG	Josh will continue the presentation with the materials shown in your second exhibit.	92	9
201404	116	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Thank you, Jane.	92	9
201404	117	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	As outlined in the upper-left panel of exhibit 2, my portion of the briefing will start with a discussion of the current state of the federal funds market and briefly note how the effective federal funds rate is constructed each day and how it is used in financial markets.	92	9
201404	118	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Then I will turn to a discussion of some of the contractual issues that could arise if the publication of the federal funds rate unexpectedly changed or ceased and highlight some of the risks that this may introduce.	92	9
201404	119	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	I will then discuss several options for preventing or mitigating the impact of these risks, including the possible consideration of alternative policy rates.	92	9
201404	120	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	I will conclude with a brief review of possible alternative target rates.	92	9
201404	121	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	First, regarding the state of the federal funds market, prior to 2008, trading activity in the fed funds market was relatively robust, with about $200 billion in trades each day across the entire fed funds market, as seen in the upper-right panel.	92	9
201404	122	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Roughly 60 percent of this activity was believed to comprise interbank borrowing and lending, with most of the remainder made up of lending by GSEs to banks.	92	9
201404	123	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	In the past few years, average daily volume has shrunk to about $60 billion, 30 percent of its pre-crisis level, with a substantial majority of the remaining activity representing one type of lending:  Federal Home Loan Banks lending to foreign banking organizations.	92	9
201404	124	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Trading in the fed funds market is conducted in two ways: directly between holders of reserve balances or via a broker.	92	9
201404	125	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	The effective federal funds rate is constructed by the Desk each morning based on data received from four of the largest brokers for all fed funds trades conducted through those brokers on the prior day.	92	9
201404	126	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	The effective rate is then published by the Desk.	92	9
201404	127	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	In addition to its role in monetary policy, the effective federal funds rate appears in a number of financial products as a reference rate.	92	9
201404	128	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Although it is much less widely used than LIBOR, the effective federal funds rate is referenced in a broad set of financial contracts and agreements, most notably fed funds futures and overnight indexed swap, or OIS, contracts.	92	9
201404	129	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	This widespread use could lead to complications if the publication of the effective federal funds rate were to unexpectedly cease or if there were a substantial change in its definition.	92	9
201404	130	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	These complications could lead to contractual disputes—most notably, claims of contract frustration.	92	9
201404	131	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Under those conditions, the financial system could face a number of potential problems, including a reduction or elimination of liquidity and significant market uncertainty related to cash flows and valuations.	92	9
201404	132	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	The scope of disruption is uncertain.	92	9
201404	133	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	For example, a change in the methodology or definition of the effective federal funds rate could create problems for existing contracts if the rate published by the Federal Reserve ceased to be viewed as consistent with the spirit of the effective fed funds rate.	92	9
201404	134	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	The relevant contract law doctrines are complex and their application is fact specific and uncertain, and so it is difficult to state the precise conditions under which changes in methodology or definition could lead to claims of contract frustration.	92	9
201404	135	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	However, on the basis of the limited set of contracts reviewed, the staff believes that the burden on a party seeking judicial modification or termination of its contract on such grounds would be high.	92	9
201404	136	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Broadly speaking, there are three developments, outlined in the middle-left panel, that could reduce the already limited volume in the federal funds market, possibly increasing the likelihood of encountering the issues that I have mentioned.	92	9
201404	137	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	First, regulatory changes could make banks less willing to borrow in the federal funds market in order to earn the IOER rate.	92	9
201404	138	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	For example, changes in regulations associated with Basel III could lead internationally active banks to find federal funds arbitrage trades unprofitable and, therefore, reduce these transactions.	92	9
201404	139	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	The second possibility is that the Federal Home Loan Banks could decide for a number of reasons to limit or even stop their lending in the federal funds market.	92	9
201404	140	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Because nearly 90 percent of the brokered fed funds market is made up of FHLBs lending to foreign banks, such a decision could greatly reduce the volume of trading.	92	9
201404	141	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Third, policies adopted during normalization could limit the federal funds activity that we currently see.	92	9
201404	142	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	For example, offering overnight reverse repos to a broad set of counterparties at rates near IOER, as is the case in some of the options that Jane highlighted, could further reduce fed funds trading volumes and lead the effective federal funds rate to become more volatile and less tightly connected to other money market rates.	92	9
201404	143	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	There are several possible policy responses to these concerns, outlined in the middle-right panel.	92	9
201404	144	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Policymakers could focus on near-term monetary policy frameworks that would not reduce the incentives for the federal funds trading that we currently see.	92	9
201404	145	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Generally speaking, these frameworks contemplate the use of an overnight reverse repo facility at a relatively wide spread in relation to IOER or no use of overnight reverse repo at all.	92	9
201404	146	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Alternatively, the Committee could change the target rate it uses to communicate policy.	92	9
201404	147	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	There are a number of possibilities in this regard, as outlined in the lower-left panel.	92	9
201404	148	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	First, the Federal Reserve could publish and use as a target a broader measure of overnight bank funding costs that would include both fed funds and Eurodollar transactions.	92	9
201404	149	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Such a rate would likely be more robust during normalization because Eurodollars trade in a larger market, as seen in the lower-right panel, with a broader range of participants.	92	9
201404	150	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Second, the Committee could choose to target a secured overnight rate, such as the rate on overnight Treasury general collateral repo.	92	9
201404	151	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	This market is substantially larger than either the federal funds or the Eurodollar market and has a broader range of participants.	92	9
201404	152	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	The Treasury repo rate is somewhat more sensitive to flight-to- quality flows than other money market rates, so if this rate were to become the policy target and the target were not reduced in the face of a flight-to-quality shock, it is possible that other money market rates could face greater upward pressure.	92	9
201404	153	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	A third option would involve targeting a broad set of short-term interest rates.	92	9
201404	154	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	The target might be specified as a range or a weighted average, or it could be left undefined.	92	9
201404	155	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	An attractive feature of such a target is that it would encompass a broad range of markets and participants.	92	9
201404	156	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	It might therefore be an attractive alternative, as it would provide some flexibility around how tightly any one interest rate should move in response to a change in the target.	92	9
201404	157	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Finally, the Committee could consider adopting an administered rate as its policy rate.	92	9
201404	158	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	This could include, for example, the IOER rate or the rate on a standing overnight reverse repo facility.	92	9
201404	159	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	A key benefit of an administered rate would be that policymakers could control it with certainty, which could be helpful in cases in which it may be operationally complex or otherwise difficult to keep a selected market rate close to the desired target.	92	9
201404	160	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	If policymakers were willing to tolerate some deviation between the administered policy rate and market rates, using an administered rate as a target could provide more flexibility during normalization, while still providing clarity on the stance of policy.	92	9
201404	161	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	Administered rates are used by other central banks, such as the Bank of England and the ECB.	92	9
201404	162	2014-04-30	meeting	FROST	With that, I’d like to turn to Fabio for a discussion of some of the financial- stability implications of a fixed-rate, full-allotment overnight reverse repo facility.	92	9
201404	163	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	Thank you, Josh.	92	9
201404	164	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	In our remarks, Antoine and I will focus on the potential financial-stability implications of a standing fixed-rate, full-allotment ON RRP facility.	92	9
201404	165	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	As indicated in the top-left panel of exhibit 3, there are potential financial-stability benefits and costs to having such a facility.	92	9
201404	166	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	The provision of a new, risk-free liquid asset, possibly in very large quantities, could support financial stability by crowding out private, seemingly safe “money-like” liabilities created by financial and nonfinancial firms.	92	9
201404	167	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	During crises, however, rapid take-up at the ON RRP facility could magnify flight-to-quality flows and contribute to a rapid decline in the availability of short-term funding for a range of private firms.	92	9
201404	168	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	As noted to the right, three recent episodes of widespread flights to quality—	92	9
201404	169	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	September 2008 and the debt-ceiling standoffs of July–August 2011 and October 2013—provide a useful illustration of the dynamics that may threaten financial stability and how an ON RRP facility might affect such flows.	92	9
201404	170	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	During these episodes, investors ran from short-term vehicles that embedded liquidity and credit risk, although the timing and severity of runs on individual instruments varied considerably.	92	9
201404	171	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	For example, in the week of September 15–19, 2008, investors redeemed $310 billion, on net, from prime MMFs, while during the debt-ceiling standoffs in 2011 and 2013 run dynamics occurred, but on a more modest scale.	92	9
201404	172	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	Safe-haven inflows were also quite large during these episodes, although destinations—which can include Treasury bills, government MMFs, and bank liquid deposits—varied.	92	9
201404	173	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	For example, government-only MMF assets and liquid deposits together increased about $300 billion in one week in September 2008.	92	9
201404	174	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	During the debt-ceiling episodes of 2011 and 2013, investors shunned some government securities and banks attracted large inflows.	92	9
201404	175	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	As indicated in the bottom-left panel, the introduction of a standing ON RRP facility could amplify some of these flight-to-quality dynamics and alter the destinations of safe-haven flows.	92	9
201404	176	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	Cash that would have moved quickly into liquid deposits—particularly at custodian banks—could go instead into the ON RRP facility—for example, through MMFs that invest in ON RRPs.	92	9
201404	177	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	The sources of flight- to-quality flows, such as prime MMFs, could experience larger outflows than in past episodes, and the availability of short-term funding for broker–dealer and nonfinancial firms through instruments like repo and CP could decline more quickly.	92	9
201404	178	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	Moreover, it is possible that additional flight-to-quality flows might occur because of the creation of a perfectly elastically supplied risk-free asset.	92	9
201404	179	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	Some potential mechanisms for such flows include greater portfolio reallocations by MMF counterparties to the ON RRP facility, larger investor shifts from prime MMFs to government MMFs that hold ON RRPs, and larger inflows to these government MMFs or directly to the ON RRP facility from other sources, including from investors abroad.	92	9
201404	180	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	As discussed in the staff memo, such flows could potentially be very large.	92	9
201404	181	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	The financial-stability implications of potentially altered flight-to-safety flows would depend in large part on the institutions and firms that lose short-term funding as investors shift to ON RRPs.	92	9
201404	182	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	For example, on average in the first quarter, MMF counterparties provided over $500 billion in private financing that matures within a week, primarily to large banks and their subsidiaries (such as broker–dealers).	92	9
201404	183	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	In addition, the redirection of cash that might have gone into liquid deposits in the past may have financial-stability implications, as the banks that received such cash would have had a broader range of options for reinvesting it than MMFs.	92	9
201404	184	2014-04-30	meeting	NATALUCCI	Antoine will now examine some facility design features that might mitigate run risks.	92	9
201404	185	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	Thanks, Fabio.	92	9
201404	186	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	In the spirit of the discussion about funding flows, I will consider in my remarks the consequences of having an ON RRP facility once a run is under way.	92	9
201404	187	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	First, it is worth noting that central bank intermediation of money markets in times of acute stress, when investors are particularly risk-averse, may be desirable.	92	9
201404	188	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	But the question is whether the adjustments could be too large or occur too rapidly, and so be disruptive.	92	9
201404	189	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	In the remainder of my presentation, I will discuss options to reduce the risk that an ON RRP facility could contribute to liquidity dislocations; specifically, lowering the interest rate offered at the facility and maintaining caps on the facility, or both.	92	9
201404	190	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	As noted in the bottom-right panel, lowering the rate at the ON RRP facility in times of crisis would make it a less attractive option, as long as market participants remain somewhat rate sensitive.	92	9
201404	191	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	But it may not be reliable enough as a standalone tool.	92	9
201404	192	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	Lowering the rate preemptively would be difficult and could send a negative signal to market participants and unintentionally trigger a run.	92	9
201404	193	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	Waiting until after a surge of investment at the facility has been observed could mean that lowering the rate happens too late.	92	9
201404	194	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	Instead, imposing permanent but adjustable caps on the facility usage, designed to rarely bind in normal times, could address the financial-stability risk effectively.	92	9
201404	195	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	The caps could be set for each investor, as is the case today, or at some aggregate amount.	92	9
201404	196	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	The cap could also be rigid, so that no investment is allowed above the cap, or flexible, with some investment allowed above the cap, but at a lower interest rate.	92	9
201404	197	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	The appropriate design would presumably depend on an assessment of the possible risks.	92	9
201404	198	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	Let me start by discussing individual versus aggregate caps.	92	9
201404	199	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	For individual caps, all counterparties could have the same fixed limit on the amount they can invest.	92	9
201404	200	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	For example, today all counterparties can invest up to $10 billion, but no more.	92	9
201404	201	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	Or each counterparty could have its own individual limit—for example, based on historical usage of the program by the counterparty.	92	9
201404	202	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	One could consider average take-up over a recent period multiplied by, say, 1.5.	92	9
201404	203	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	A counterparty that has invested $6 billion, on average, in the past would, thus, have a cap of $9 billion.	92	9
201404	204	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	The main benefit of individual caps is that counterparties know exactly how much they can invest.	92	9
201404	205	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	In contrast, an aggregate cap would specify the maximum amount of total investment.	92	9
201404	206	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	For example, it could specify that total take-up at the facility cannot exceed $200 billion.	92	9
201404	207	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	In the rare instances in which the sum of the bids exceeds the cap, the bids would have to be rationed in some manner.	92	9
201404	208	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	The main benefit of an aggregate cap is that it would likely be tighter than the sum of individual caps.	92	9
201404	209	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	Let me turn now to rigid versus flexible caps.	92	9
201404	210	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	A rigid cap could not be breached, as is the case today.	92	9
201404	211	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	A counterparty cannot invest more than $10 billion at the facility.	92	9
201404	212	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	A flexible cap could allow some investment above the cap but at a lower rate—conceivably, at a negative rate.	92	9
201404	213	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	For example, a counterparty could be allowed to invest more than $10 billion, but each dollar above that amount would earn 15 basis points less than the current rate of 5 basis points, or negative 10 basis points.	92	9
201404	214	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	An aggregate flexible cap would work along the same lines.	92	9
201404	215	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	In all cases, the cap could be adjusted over time.	92	9
201404	216	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	What is the best design for a cap?	92	9
201404	217	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	This could depend on what risk you are most concerned about.	92	9
201404	218	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	If your main concern is to have a tight cap, to limit the potential for very rapid increases in take-up, then a rigid aggregate cap may be appealing.	92	9
201404	219	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	If your main concern is allowing some flexibility for the provision of a safe asset in a crisis, then flexible individual caps may be appealing.	92	9
201404	220	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	It seems likely that a well-designed system of caps could significantly reduce the financial-stability risks posed by an ON RRP facility in a crisis.	92	9
201404	221	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	The final page of your handout shows the discussion questions that was distributed with the cover memo for the normalization memos.	92	9
201404	222	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	You may want to address these questions in your comments during the go-round.	92	9
201404	223	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	Thank you, that completes our prepared remarks.	92	9
201404	224	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	We’d be happy to take your questions.	92	9

201404	246	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	One thing to say first is that the estimate is going to depend on what you think the frictions are that are keeping market rates lower than the IOER rate.	92	9
201404	247	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	For example, if you think that the reason interest rates are low is predominantly due to balance sheet costs, then lowering the spread between the IOER and overnight RRP rates means that you are going to see an increase in take-up.	92	9

201404	299	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	You’d set the repo rate equal to the IOER rate.	92	9
201404	300	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Take-up is unpredictable, as you just discussed, but you put a cap on at some fairly large size that the Committee is comfortable with.	92	9
201404	301	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Is there anything wrong with that case, or are there good and bad aspects of that case?	92	9
201404	302	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	To the extent that we think that banks are really facing balance sheet costs and that you put a cap in so that these balance sheet costs don’t get eliminated, then you have different costs that different financial institutions are facing, and you would imagine that banks are going to take some kind of evasive actions in order to reduce those costs or in order to be more competitive.	92	9
201404	303	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	And so you’re likely not to have a level playing field, and I think we would be concerned about that.	92	9

201404	311	2014-04-30	meeting	ENGLISH	If I could follow up for a moment, I think there are two issues that the Committee would have to trade off in that case.	92	9
201404	312	2014-04-30	meeting	ENGLISH	One is that if the rate on the overnight RRPs were the same as the IOER rate, for the reason of the FDIC premium costs and other costs the banks face, you might end up with a whole lot of overnight RRPs and not a lot of reserves.	92	9
201404	313	2014-04-30	meeting	ENGLISH	If you put a cap on, then you’d have to ration who gets the overnight RRPs and who doesn’t because the rate would be at a level that would lead to extra demand for the overnight RRPs.	92	9
201404	314	2014-04-30	meeting	ENGLISH	The other factor that you’d have to think about is that if you set a high cap—if you had a whole lot of overnight RRPs—you’d be doing a whole lot of transacting and a whole lot of your policy implementation through the nonbank part of the financial sector.	92	9
201404	315	2014-04-30	meeting	ENGLISH	I think some parts of the Committee might be unhappy with that—operating so much with money funds and with GSEs, and not operating in the traditional arena, which is the banking sector.	92	9
201404	316	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Two-hander?	92	9
201404	317	2014-04-30	meeting	STEIN	Actually, it’s a direct follow-up to this, if I might.	92	9

201404	499	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	It’s safe; the Fed can return the money to them.	92	9
201404	500	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	In some severe states of the world, their private counterparty might not be able to return the money to them.	92	9
201404	501	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	And people become very rate insensitive.	92	9
201404	502	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	—which we saw in September 2008.	92	9
201404	503	2014-04-30	meeting	ENGLISH	One point that was in the memo and that, in my view, is important is that you want these mitigants—whatever they are, caps, rates that move because of auction approaches or whatever—to always be in place.	92	9
201404	504	2014-04-30	meeting	ENGLISH	You don’t want there to be a switch that somebody has to turn because that is then very bad news, potentially, for market participants.	92	9
201404	505	2014-04-30	meeting	ENGLISH	So you want it to be part of the furniture.	92	9
201404	506	2014-04-30	meeting	ENGLISH	Maybe these things hit at the end of every quarter, when we know that usage of this thing is going to go up.	92	9
201404	507	2014-04-30	meeting	ENGLISH	So it just becomes something that we are used to and isn’t that big a deal.	92	9

201404	521	2014-04-30	meeting	STEIN	I think, Bill, what you were just describing sounds like an auction in which you are basically, on every single day, auctioning off something like 120 percent of what you expect the demand to be, and you have a reserve price.	92	9
201404	522	2014-04-30	meeting	STEIN	So on a normal day, you are just hitting the reserve price.	92	9

201404	541	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	As some of you have heard me point out before, we were founded to provide a monetary instrument for people to use when the supply of that instrument was inelastic—when they wanted to get their deposits out and have hand-to-hand currency to carry around.	92	9
201404	542	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	It was well known at the time that there were structural, legal impediments to the elastic supply of currency under the National Bank Act.	92	9
201404	543	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	We were founded to provide that elastic supply of currency to people panicking who were taking their money out of banks.	92	9
201404	544	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	So I agree with President Kocherlakota that it’s just odd and a bit dissonant to be thinking about limiting that flow.	92	9
201404	545	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	Thinking about the parallel with our founding caused to spring to my mind a question about why you would restrict a flight to safety.	92	9
201404	546	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	The broad philosophy here seems to be that we can help financial stability by taking off the table or limiting the size of one of the array of options that fleers have to flee to.	92	9
201404	547	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	They have other options to flee to.	92	9

201404	553	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	That’s the financial-stability cost that we see if the overnight RRP facility really is a perfectly elastic supply of that safe asset.	92	9

201404	629	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman Dudley.	92	9
201404	630	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Let me give you my take on this, which I hope will clarify things a little bit, at least for me.	92	9
201404	631	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I agree with President Lacker that, if people want safe assets and we provide them with those safe assets, that’s probably utility enhancing as opposed to utility reducing.	92	9
201404	632	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	But if we supply them safe assets at a fixed price, what’s going to happen in this new regime is that the prices of risky assets are going to go down, interest rates in the economy are going to go up, and financial conditions are going to tighten as a consequence of this flow.	92	9
201404	633	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	The difference between the old regime and this new regime would be that in the old regime yields on risk-free assets fall and those on risky assets go up, but they both move.	92	9
201404	634	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	In this new regime, the yield on risk-free assets doesn’t go down, and so the yield on risky assets goes up by more.	92	9
201404	635	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So you get a tightening of financial conditions.	92	9
201404	636	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s the financial-stability negative that we have to think about.	92	9
201404	637	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, you could respond to it by living with it.	92	9
201404	638	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	You could respond to it by adding reserves through doing repurchase agreements.	92	9
201404	639	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	You could respond to it by lowering your interest rate structure.	92	9
201404	640	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	But I think that the initial reaction, relative to the current regime, would be a tightening of financial conditions, and that’s really the consequence on the other side.	92	9
201404	641	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	But, Bill, we always cut rates when something like that happens.	92	9
201404	642	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Well, that would be an option.	92	9

201404	646	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I think the financial-stability issues are really quite complicated because there’s a good, in the sense that you’re offering an asset that they want to hold, which is utility enhancing, but there’s a bad—there’s a temporary tightening of financial conditions that you would be concerned about.	92	9
201404	647	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	And the question is, what’s the best way to address that?	92	9

201404	713	2014-04-30	meeting	ENGLISH	It does have the advantage that then the overnight RRP is allocated across participants more efficiently, whereas if you have an aggregate cap and some way of allocating through an auction or something, as Jeremy was talking about earlier, it’s a more efficient system.	92	9

201404	976	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	We discussed the segregated balance accounts at some length at a previous meeting, but they got a little less attention so far in these memos.	92	9
201404	977	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	They were called reserve collateral accounts at that time, but we changed the name of them.	92	9
201404	978	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	You might just want to describe quickly what they are, Antoine.	92	9
201404	979	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	Right.	92	9
201404	980	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	A segregated balance account is a specific kind of account that can be created between a bank and essentially any counterparty, pending a legal opinion by the Board’s General Counsel.	92	9
201404	981	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	This allows the investor to lend to that bank, and the reserves that correspond to that loan are segregated in a way that the bank cannot use them, and it protects the investor’s loan so there’s no counterparty risk  And automatically the next day the loan is sent back so that the investor gets his funds back.	92	9
201404	982	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	The intent of that construct is to eliminate counterparty risk so as to create more competition.	92	9
201404	983	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	That way current investors who are only looking to lend to FBOs and large domestic banks would be more willing to lend to a wide variety of banks.	92	9
201404	984	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	And it does, as you suggested, create a competitive rate because banks are competing with each other in order to offer these accounts, and we would expect that to lower the wedge between market rates and the IOER rate.	92	9
201404	985	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	We haven’t completely thought through all of the financial-stability implications.	92	9
201404	986	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	In many ways, at a high enough level, they look a lot like an overnight RRP construct, but we would not be direct counterparties, and the rate would not be set administratively.	92	9
201404	987	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	So I think you’re right to suggest that banks would want to lower the rates in times of crisis.	92	9
201404	988	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	We might also want to think about whether there are possibilities, or it’s desirable, to have other mitigants, like caps, to avoid surges.	92	9
201404	989	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	But these would be private-sector arrangements, so banks and their investors would decide, maybe constrained by some limits we impose on them, how much you can increase your investment in a segregated balance account from one day to the next, or some of these considerations.	92	9
201404	990	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	So we would avoid some of the problems that President Kocherlakota was worried about in that earlier discussion, in that it would not look like we were limiting the ability of people to move into an account.	92	9
201404	991	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Really, the cap becomes the amount of excess reserves at any one institution and that institution’s ability to find a counterparty.	92	9
201404	992	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	Right.	92	9
201404	993	2014-04-30	meeting	MARTIN	We need to think more about this because we didn’t get a chance in this set of memos to really investigate the segregated balance accounts.	92	9
