201404	1476	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	92	9
201404	1477	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201404	1478	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you very much to the staff for all the memos that you provided.	92	9
201404	1479	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	It certainly has been thought-provoking, and I think this morning’s discussion as well as the memos have probably answered some of our questions and then raised a few more, but thank you very much for that.	92	9
201404	1480	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Like Vice Chairman Dudley and President Fisher, I’m starting with some guiding principles and then I’ll answer the questions.	92	9
201404	1481	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	The first principle, I think, is very similar to theirs.	92	9
201404	1482	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	We should choose an option in which we are highly confident we’ll be able to raise short-term rates when we view that as appropriate.	92	9
201404	1483	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	The reputational risk to the Federal Reserve from adopting a new instrument that does not have the desired relationship with short-term rates would greatly complicate exit strategies.	92	9
201404	1484	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	The second one that President Kocherlakota kind of alluded to, which I don’t think was as emphasized in the memos, is that we should remain focused on achieving the appropriate macroeconomic outcomes.	92	9
201404	1485	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	When we choose to tighten policy, we should choose our policy instruments in large part with an eye toward how effectively they influence the broader financial conditions we care most about.	92	9
201404	1486	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Third, we should realize that we will still be learning by doing, because we have never before had such a large balance sheet.	92	9
201404	1487	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	This would argue for a cautious approach when we initiate the first tightening, recognizing that the size of the take-up of the reverse repo facility, the volatility of that take-up, and the market reaction to our action are all quite uncertain.	92	9
201404	1488	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I was ready to cross that out if I had gotten a different answer to my question, but it stayed in.	92	9
201404	1489	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	The fourth one is that we should remain open to changing our tactics as we learn more about operating with a large balance sheet as the balance sheet evolves.	92	9
201404	1490	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Our previous exit principles evolved significantly as our strategies evolved.	92	9
201404	1491	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Hence, an important part of the exit strategy should be an acknowledgment that it may change, not only as economic situations change, but also as we learn from implementing the new policies.	92	9
201404	1492	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Fifth, we have used the size and composition of the balance sheet as important tools for generating appropriate macroeconomic outcomes.	92	9
201404	1493	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	We should maintain the flexibility to continue to use these tools.	92	9
201404	1494	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	And, sixth, whether or not the federal funds market is robust in the short run seems less important than our ability to effectively influence short-term rates more generally.	92	9
201404	1495	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	In terms of the questions that were addressed to the Committee—first question, during the period of normalization, I would focus on how effectively our policies raise short-term rates generally rather than focus on the federal funds market.	92	9
201404	1496	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	As long as we have a sizable balance sheet, the federal funds market is likely to be somewhat idiosyncratic, and the behavior of the federal funds market will likely be sensitive to the size of the reverse repo facility, which will be quite uncertain with an open allotment.	92	9
201404	1497	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	For question two, I would initially focus our discussion on the interest rates we control, the interest rate on excess reserves and the reverse repo rate.	92	9
201404	1498	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Because these are new tools, there’s a high degree of uncertainty about how market rates will respond to our setting of these administered rates.	92	9
201404	1499	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Once we have some experience with how market rates respond, we should revisit this issue.	92	9
201404	1500	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	On the third question, we should have an open mind about how we utilize the fixed-rate, open-allotment, reverse repo facility in the long run.	92	9
201404	1501	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	We may find it to be an effective and important permanent tool depending on what our experience is through the normalization.	92	9
201404	1502	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	And for question four, I would initially begin with a very large spread between the reverse repo rate and the interest rate on excess reserves, similar to the spreads we currently see between short-term rates and the interest rate on excess reserves.	92	9
201404	1503	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	As we develop a better understanding of how the size and volatility of the take-up is affected by the spread, we may want to narrow the spread over time.	92	9
201404	1504	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would want to keep the spread large enough to minimize the likelihood of hitting the caps we are likely to need when we set the program.	92	9
201404	1505	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	As we gain experience with how the size of the take-up is related to risk-on periods and the term structure of interest rates, we’ll be able to determine the appropriate spread.	92	9
201404	1506	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Regarding question five, our focus should remain solidly on achieving appropriate macroeconomic outcomes.	92	9
201404	1507	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Concerns about the financial costs of the various options in terms of the interest cost for the Federal Reserve should remain secondary to concerns about our ability to influence key short-term rates that are linked to households’ and firms’ economic decisions and, thus, to our ability to achieve our fundamental macroeconomic objectives.	92	9
201404	1508	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Sixth, while I have an open mind, my preferred options would not be options 1, 4, or 5 during the normalization period.	92	9
201404	1509	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I currently prefer an option somewhat between options 2 and 3, though I could obviously change that preference as we learn more through the next year.	92	9
201404	1510	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	As I said a moment ago, I would keep an open mind as to the appropriate operating procedure in the long run and wait to make any long-term decisions until we have a better understanding of the normalization process.	92	9
201404	1511	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Finally, for question seven, while it is essential that we do some testing of the reverse repo facility to better understand its effects on short-term interest rates, I would wait to do large- scale testing of the facility until we have finished the taper.	92	9
201404	1512	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	My concern is that such a large-scale testing could be interpreted by market participants as signaling a tightening before we intend to do so.	92	9
201404	1513	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	I suggest that at the end of the taper, we gradually raise the reverse repo rate above the current level of the federal funds rate, but still below the IOER rate, possibly up to 10 basis points, to obtain a better understanding of how the facility works.	92	9
201404	1514	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	After that, we might want the first restrictive rate increase to be small.	92	9
201404	1515	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	For example, we could move the interest on excess reserves to 35 basis points, leaving the reverse repo rate at 10 basis points, to obtain a better understanding of the relationship between the interest rate on excess reserves and the reverse repurchase facility.	92	9
201404	1516	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	So I would start off pretty tentative, get a better understanding of some of the uncertainties that we still have, and once we learn from doing that, then I would proceed depending on what we learned from that exercise.	92	9
201404	1517	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201404	1518	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you very much.	92	9
201404	1519	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	President Williams.	92	9
201404	1520	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201404	1521	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Well, over the intermeeting period it seemed that winter finally arrived on the West Coast in the form of a blizzard of memos.	92	9
201404	1522	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	[Laughter]	92	9
201404	1523	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Still, I, too, really appreciate the staff’s hard work on these important issues, and I’m actually going to give a principle-free discussion of this topic, and I’m going to answer the questions as part of my discussion.	92	9
201404	1524	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	So Simon, you’re going to have to take careful notes.	92	9
201404	1525	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I have two bottom-line takeaways.	92	9
201404	1526	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The first is that we should continue to target the federal funds rate, appropriately modified to include the broader set of transactions in the overnight interbank lending market during normalization.	92	9
201404	1527	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	And the second is that we need a much better understanding of the issues before committing to a longer-run operating framework.	92	9
201404	1528	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think I’ve already heard this said many times.	92	9
201404	1529	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	But that implies that we should not take any near-term action that forecloses options in the future.	92	9
201404	1530	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’m going to elaborate on each point.	92	9
201404	1531	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	First, by continuing to use the federal funds rate as our headline policy instrument, we will greatly facilitate policy communication during the normalization period.	92	9
201404	1532	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The federal funds rate may not be perfect and isn’t perfect, but it is familiar, and before we can consider safely shifting to a new instrument, we need further experimentation and a greater understanding of the consequences, both intended and unintended.	92	9
201404	1533	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In particular, the discussion today has made it clear that although we’ve made substantial progress in testing alternative tools, there are still many important unresolved issues.	92	9
201404	1534	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The overnight reverse repo facility has worked fairly well at putting a floor under short-term money market rates, and I support further testing, particularly with an eye toward learning how the reverse repo facility affects the functioning of the interbank lending market.	92	9
201404	1535	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	There is some worry that the fed funds rate will decouple from other short-term interest rates, potentially in a nonlinear fashion as the reverse repo rate rises toward the IOER rate.	92	9
201404	1536	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	That would pose a potential risk to our communications strategy.	92	9
201404	1537	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	More experience with testing that tool can help clarify this risk.	92	9
201404	1538	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	While I’m in favor of additional reverse repo tests, with the goal of using this tool actively during the transition period, I’m inclined to put the Term Deposit Facility and term reverse repos on the back burner.	92	9
201404	1539	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think the IOER rate and the overnight reverse repo facility will give us plenty of control over short rates for implementing monetary policy.	92	9
201404	1540	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The term tool should only be needed as a backup to be called upon if our other tools fall short.	92	9
201404	1541	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Looking ahead over the next couple of years, I’m confident that we will quickly learn to fine-tune our approach once it’s implemented.	92	9
201404	1542	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The control of interest rates will rapidly improve as we gain experience with adjusting interest rates in the context of a large balance sheet and learn to calibrate our procedures appropriately.	92	9
201404	1543	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	One practical path forward would be to continue to set a target range for the fed funds rate using the overnight reverse repo and IOER rates as implementation tools.	92	9
201404	1544	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The calculation of the fed funds rate could obviously be modified to include Eurodollar rates to reduce the sensitivity to idiosyncratic factors, as described in the memo.	92	9
201404	1545	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	With experience, we’ll learn the best procedure for setting the overnight reverse repo and IOER rates or spreads to keep the new, improved fed funds rate near the center of the target range.	92	9
201404	1546	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Over time, as our understanding of this new approach improves, we could narrow the target range for the federal funds rate or move back to a single value for the target rate.	92	9
201404	1547	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	My second point is that we don’t need to commit to a long-term operating framework today.	92	9
201404	1548	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The corridor system has served us well in the past.	92	9
201404	1549	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	All short-term interest rates have moved together very closely, especially if you look at them on a monthly-average basis, which is enough for effective policy control.	92	9
201404	1550	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	It’s possible that the floor system could work even better at some point in the fairly distant future, but both the political and financial-stability risks could be sizable.	92	9
201404	1551	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Again, we’ll be able to gather some useful information on these issues during the transition period over the next several years.	92	9
201404	1552	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Importantly, as I said at the start, because we’ll be learning over time, we should not take any near-term action that closes off our options in the future.	92	9
201404	1553	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	To my mind, this rules out the adoption of option 1 and perhaps option 2 because they could irrevocably damage the federal funds market.	92	9
201404	1554	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you.	92	9
201404	1555	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201404	1556	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	President Lockhart.	92	9
201404	1557	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201404	1558	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Like everyone else, my thanks to the staff for a very impressive spectrum of memos that were very helpful.	92	9
201404	1559	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I thought you framed the discussion well as a starting point in a process of refining the Committee’s approach, laid out the considerations and the tradeoffs, and pointed out the need for further testing, all of which I agree with.	92	9
201404	1560	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Due to the preliminary nature of today’s discussion, I am not going to present hard-and- fast conclusions on the questions raised.	92	9
201404	1561	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Rather, I would like to share how I’m framing my thinking and how I’m leaning on the key tradeoffs.	92	9
201404	1562	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	In effect, what I’ll present are my priors ahead of the Q&A discussion that just took place.	92	9
201404	1563	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	In reaction to the material in the staff memos, I am organizing my thinking by applying three tests to the five policy implementation approaches.	92	9
201404	1564	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	The tests are control of overnight and short-term interest rates, communication ease and effectiveness, and serviceability of the approach over time.	92	9
201404	1565	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Let me flesh these out a little bit.	92	9
201404	1566	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I favor approaches that seem to convey a high certainty of control over the policy rate and establish a relatively hard floor, especially in the first stages of normalization.	92	9
201404	1567	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	The underlying principle is:  Don’t take a lot of risk with FOMC and policy credibility in the beginning.	92	9
201404	1568	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	With regard to communication, I favor approaches that I can envision explaining without excessive contortions, both as an approach and in the particulars of Committee decisions, to both financial practitioners and the general public.	92	9
201404	1569	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	With regard to serviceability over time, the chosen approach should be durable to the extent possible.	92	9
201404	1570	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I think we can probably preserve needed tactical flexibility or optionality within a scheme that varies the emphasis on tools, as contingencies dictate or conditions change, including the scale of the balance sheet.	92	9
201404	1571	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	In that respect, I think it’s important to communicate at the outset that we’re not changing the theoretical framework of policy implementation and that our approach continues the focus on the usual transmission mechanism of influence over a broad array of market rates through direct influence on short-term rates.	92	9
201404	1572	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I think it’s possible that the federal funds market might become more viable as a monetary control mechanism as the balance sheet shrinks.	92	9
201404	1573	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	It might make sense, in my thinking, to de-emphasize the federal funds rate at the outset, for reasons that are well described in the staff memo, but to try to preserve its functioning with the idea of returning it to a more central role later on.	92	9
201404	1574	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	However, I don’t envision us holding to the centrality of the fed funds rate target in the early stages of normalization.	92	9
201404	1575	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Now, to get a little bit more specific regarding the options, I lean toward options 1, 2, and 3, versus options 4 and 5.	92	9
201404	1576	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I think it’s advisable to establish a hard floor through emphasis on administered-rate setting through the IOER rate and the overnight reverse repo rate.	92	9
201404	1577	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I think there is something to be said for the simplicity of option 1 with the IOER and reverse repo rates equal, as they are basically equivalent assets, but I don’t dismiss the concerns about financial stability.	92	9
201404	1578	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I am inclined to think that some sort of allotment-cap approach might reasonably address this concern.	92	9
201404	1579	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I would like to see further work done on the financial-stability concerns before we decide the very important question of differentiated or equivalent IOER and reverse repo rates.	92	9
201404	1580	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	The balance sheet may stay quite large for quite some time, so I’m skeptical about the effectiveness of the term draining tools as a way to exert complete enough direct monetary control.	92	9
201404	1581	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	As I read them, with their reliance on draining operations, options 4 and 5 may present challenges.	92	9
201404	1582	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Longer term, a viable federal funds market that provides a daily market signal of demand for reserves seems to me to be worth preserving.	92	9
201404	1583	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	In that sense, option 3 is attractive.	92	9
201404	1584	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	The viability of the funds market is a still-open and pivotal question, in my view.	92	9
201404	1585	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	What are the control risks inherent in running a policy with emphasis on a small federal funds market dominated, at least in the beginning, by the Home Loan Banks?	92	9
201404	1586	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Would a policy change by the Home Loan Banks throw a wrench into option 3?	92	9
201404	1587	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Is the control risk associated with trying to maintain the fed funds rate as having a central role worth accepting?	92	9
201404	1588	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I would appreciate more staff work and discussion on these subjects.	92	9
201404	1589	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	It does seem to me that the staff has tried to set out distinct options for the sake of discussion, but combinations that involve mixes and matches are feasible.	92	9
201404	1590	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	It is not clear to me that some use of the term draining tools could not be in the mix while implementing something like options 1, 2, or 3.	92	9
201404	1591	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	So I do not object to further testing of the Term Deposit Facility.	92	9
201404	1592	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Overall, in response to the exercises presented, I settle mostly on option 2, maybe option 3, with more confidence that the fed funds rate won’t behave idiosyncratically.	92	9
201404	1593	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201404	1594	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201404	1595	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	92	9
201404	1596	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201404	1597	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I’m going to divide my comments into two parts.	92	9
201404	1598	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	The first part will be about how the exit strategy is related to the tactical issues discussed in the staff memos, and the second part will be to walk through the questions posed and give my perspective on those questions.	92	9
201404	1599	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	So let’s start with relation to the exit strategy.	92	9
201404	1600	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	As many of you know, I have advocated in the past a different exit strategy than the one that is outlined in the Committee’s statement of exit principles.	92	9
201404	1601	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	In particular, I have suggested that a LIFO exit strategy may be preferable for the Committee.	92	9
201404	1602	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	LIFO means last in, first out.	92	9
201404	1603	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I suggested that the Committee’s more controversial and experimental policies could be reversed first, as they were attempts by the Committee to provide accommodation after the zero lower bound was encountered in December of 2008.	92	9
201404	1604	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	In particular, the balance sheet should first be allowed to shrink, but at a carefully controlled pace, and the pace of balance sheet reduction would become, for a time, the primary tool of the Committee, just as the pace of balance sheet expansion is at the present time.	92	9
201404	1605	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Even before revising the size of the balance sheet, LIFO would call for the reversal of the Operation Twist program put in place by the Committee in 2011.	92	9
201404	1606	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	The LIFO policy would have the great advantage that the Committee could take action to remove accommodation without raising the policy rate.	92	9
201404	1607	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	The policy rate could stay much lower for much longer.	92	9
201404	1608	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	At some point in the distant future, under a LIFO approach, the balance sheet would approach a more normal size and further removal of accommodation would have to come from increases in the policy rate.	92	9
201404	1609	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	However, with the balance sheet back to a normal size, the Committee would then be able to resume targeting the federal funds rate, if it so desired, or it could turn to targeting another short-term interest rate, such as the repo rate.	92	9
201404	1610	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	But the complications of trying to maintain the large balance sheet and still influence the federal funds rate would be eliminated.	92	9
201404	1611	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	An open question, then, about what we’re talking about today, is what are we doing with balance sheet policy as we are thinking about raising the fed funds rate?	92	9
201404	1612	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Is the balance sheet staying constant, or is it being reduced?	92	9
201404	1613	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	If it’s being reduced, isn’t that tightening policy?	92	9
201404	1614	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	If it’s not tightening policy, then was balance sheet expansion not easing policy?	92	9
201404	1615	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I think there are some logical difficulties with some of what we’re thinking about here in trying to deal with the policy rate issue separately from the balance sheet question.	92	9
201404	1616	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	The Committee may wish to reconsider some aspects of the LIFO exit strategy in light of the discussion in the staff memos concerning normalization of a large balance sheet.	92	9
201404	1617	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	In general, the LIFO exit strategy has much to commend it in view of the many technical issues the Committee now faces in trying to eventually raise the level of short-term nominal interest rates in the United States.	92	9
201404	1618	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	The logic of first returning to our original pre-crisis, pre-unconventional policy situation before eventually attempting policy rate liftoff seems quite compelling to me.	92	9
201404	1619	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	If we wish to remain with the current strategy, which calls for attempting to raise the policy rate before any balance sheet reduction has been attempted, then the long list of questions posed at the end of the first staff memo becomes relevant.	92	9
201404	1620	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Let me now turn to those questions.	92	9
201404	1621	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	As a general remark, I think that the questions posed refer to issues that are of only second-order importance relative to the principal macroeconomic issue, which is control or substantial influence over short-term interest rates in the US economy.	92	9
201404	1622	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	As the staff memo states, “Policymakers can be confident that they will be able to raise money market rates when the time to do so arrives, and that they will subsequently be able to exercise reasonable control over rates.”	92	9
201404	1623	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	There is, however, one issue that may be of first-order importance, which is the financial- stability question, and I will refer to this question in just a moment.	92	9
201404	1624	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Let me turn to question 1:  Should the Committee continue to target the federal funds rate during the period of normalization?	92	9
201404	1625	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	With a large balance sheet, I do not think the federal funds rate is a practical option as a target policy rate.	92	9
201404	1626	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	The federal funds market is essentially meaningless as it exists today.	92	9
201404	1627	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Nor is it likely to gain economic meaning in the medium term.	92	9
201404	1628	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I see it as somewhat detrimental to the Committee’s credibility to claim that it is this particular short-term nominal interest rate that we are most concerned about.	92	9
201404	1629	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I have also been influenced by the arguments that the Committee should try to influence a short-term nominal interest rate with more economic meaning, such as repo, which is decided in a thicker market with many more players trading.	92	9
201404	1630	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I like the following analogy.	92	9
201404	1631	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Suppose we are trying to influence the general price of fruit by intervening in the market for apples.	92	9
201404	1632	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	One way to do this would be to buy apples from, or sell apples to, a particular grocery store at a particular location in the country until the desired level of general fruit prices was obtained.	92	9
201404	1633	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Given the way economic theory works, in principle, by arbitrage this would work to achieve the objective.	92	9
201404	1634	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	But in practice, I think it would work much, much better to trade apples with a wide variety of grocery stores across the country.	92	9
201404	1635	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Something similar is going on with repo rates versus the federal funds rate, and to some extent with respect to the interest on excess reserves, which applies only to a limited set of institutions itself.	92	9
201404	1636	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Question 2.	92	9
201404	1637	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	In shifting away from the federal funds rate, would you support the development of a more robust measure of the overnight, unsecured bank funding rate to serve as a target?	92	9
201404	1638	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I think that this may be a difficult road to go down.	92	9
201404	1639	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Suppose we wanted to create an index of three different rates.	92	9
201404	1640	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	If the three different rates move in lockstep due to a robust arbitrage environment, there would be nothing to gain from aggregating the three rates.	92	9
201404	1641	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	But if the strength of arbitrage were variable among the three rates, then the changes in the strength of arbitrage would show up as variability in the index, creating an undesirable barometer of the stance of policy.	92	9
201404	1642	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	The index may move because the strength of arbitrage has changed and not because the policy stance has changed.	92	9
201404	1643	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	For these reasons, I think that the creation of such an index may be problematic.	92	9
201404	1644	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	On the sub-question of “an administered rate versus a market rate,” my staff questioned the meaning of these terms.	92	9
201404	1645	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	We should be thinking in terms of the policy rule associated with a particular rate—that is, how the rate will be adjusted in reaction to economic developments—not whether we can label a particular rule as a market rate or as an administered rate.	92	9
201404	1646	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	My staff said that a Taylor rule is really an administered rate—or is it a market rate?—because you are setting the target in reaction to developments in the economy, and that is informing the equilibrium of the economy.	92	9
201404	1647	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	So they found this distinction to be moot.	92	9
201404	1648	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Question 3.	92	9
201404	1649	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Are you supportive of a fixed-rate, full-allotment, overnight RRP facility?	92	9
201404	1650	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I’m generally supportive, although I’m anxious to hear the views of others on the Committee.	92	9
201404	1651	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I like the arguments about broader coverage, as I just mentioned.	92	9
201404	1652	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I see the IOER as covering an increasingly narrow segment of the US financial intermediation sector, as President Fisher was talking about earlier today.	92	9
201404	1653	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I will consider arguments about the appropriate spread, but in general, I think the spread of zero would be a good place to start.	92	9
201404	1654	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	That would be option 1.	92	9
201404	1655	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	And then we could use caps if we are concerned about the uptake issue.	92	9
201404	1656	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I think if repo came to be seen as the main focus of policy, FOMC communication would be sharp and effective.	92	9
201404	1657	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	There would be little doubt in the markets about where the FOMC stands.	92	9
201404	1658	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Question 4.	92	9
201404	1659	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	How much of a divergence between the IOER rate and the federal funds rate should be allowed?	92	9
201404	1660	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I saw this as a second-order issue if the federal funds rate is not a meaningful rate.	92	9
201404	1661	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	We should be thinking in terms of reducing focus on the federal funds rate.	92	9
201404	1662	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Question 5.	92	9
201404	1663	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Large net interest expense may be associated with some options.	92	9
201404	1664	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	How comfortable are you with this?	92	9
201404	1665	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I’m definitely not comfortable with the expense aspect of several of the options.	92	9
201404	1666	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I would like sharper estimates of these costs.	92	9
201404	1667	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Because I am willing to simply sell assets, if necessary, I question the idea of incurring substantial costs in order to be able to keep the large balance sheet.	92	9
201404	1668	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	If it is expensive to keep the large balance sheet, why keep it?	92	9
201404	1669	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Question 6.	92	9
201404	1670	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	If all approaches work equally well, which would you prefer?	92	9
201404	1671	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	If they all work equally well, one differentiator between the various approaches may be the financial- stability issue.	92	9
201404	1672	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I have already mentioned that this is a first-order concern for the Committee.	92	9
201404	1673	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	I certainly agree that we do not want to be encouraging or exacerbating financial instability through the adoption of an operating regime during the normalization process for monetary policy.	92	9
201404	1674	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	However, I see existing theories and ideas on this matter as insufficiently developed to give us clear guidance as to whether a particular operating regime during the normalization process is likely to enhance or reduce the probability of entering into a financial crisis in the future.	92	9
201404	1675	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	In such theories, much would depend on other actions the Federal Reserve might take to reduce the probability of a crisis or to mitigate a crisis once one develops, quite apart from the choice of a temporary operating regime itself.	92	9
201404	1676	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	My judgment is that we should not make choices on operating regimes based on the possible implications for financial stability, even though this is a first-order concern for the Committee generally.	92	9
201404	1677	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	And finally, on question 7, additional testing.	92	9
201404	1678	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	In general, I am comfortable with additional testing as suggested in the memos.	92	9
201404	1679	2014-04-30	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201404	1680	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you, President Bullard.	92	9
201404	1681	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	President Plosser.	92	9
201404	1682	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201404	1683	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Like everyone else, I want to thank the staff for the outstanding memos.	92	9
201404	1684	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	It was a lot of reading, but they were very informative and useful.	92	9
201404	1685	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	And thanks to you, Madam Chair, for our discussion this morning; I thought it was a great opportunity to have people talk about a lot of different things.	92	9
201404	1686	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I thought it was very helpful and a productive session.	92	9
201404	1687	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	As I said last meeting, my gut reaction tells me that it’s very hard to talk about tactical adjustments when we don’t know where we’re going.	92	9
201404	1688	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I used the phrase “Yogi Berra” last time, when I said that you’ve got to be careful if you don’t know where you’re going because you might end up somewhere else.	92	9
201404	1689	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	And I think we have to be careful about that, but, unfortunately, it’s pretty clear that the Committee isn’t ready to make that kind of long-run decision about where we end up, and I understand that.	92	9
201404	1690	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	So that means my guiding principle in the meantime, much as I think Vice Chairman Dudley suggested, is that as we decide among these options on the table, we don’t want to pick options for the near-term tactical decisions that would preclude our options in the future.	92	9
201404	1691	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	So we need to keep our options available to us.	92	9
201404	1692	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think our goal today should be to try to eliminate some of the options that have limited support, so we can focus more exclusively on those that are feasible and perhaps promising and do more study on those.	92	9
201404	1693	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I will give my own preference for the long run.	92	9
201404	1694	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	My own long-run preference is for us to return to something that looks like a corridor operating framework, with some market or interbank interest rate as our target in the corridor, and with the Federal Reserve holding a relatively small portfolio comprised mostly of short-term Treasuries.	92	9
201404	1695	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	This framework is consistent with the exit strategy principles we laid out in June 2011.	92	9
201404	1696	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	So I don’t really favor any option in the short run that would preclude us getting to that as our long-run operating arrangement, because as I said, that sort of corridor system worked well for us in the past.	92	9
201404	1697	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Yes, during the crisis and with our large balance sheet, things have changed.	92	9
201404	1698	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	But there is no reason that that system couldn’t work well for us in the future as the balance sheet shrinks.	92	9
201404	1699	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think the other thing to keep in mind is that, as President Lacker made clear, monetary policy is more than just control over the precision of the short-term interest rate.	92	9
201404	1700	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Monetary policy decisions tend to look like a path of interest rates, and so we could become too obsessed with movements in the short-run rate, if we’re not careful, and let that guide our decision.	92	9
201404	1701	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think we need to keep that in mind; that was a good caution on his part.	92	9
201404	1702	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	With these caveats in mind, my own assessment is that I rule out option 1, which involves a full-allotment, overnight reverse repo facility rate that equals the IOER rate.	92	9
201404	1703	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Even if we choose to rule out option 1 now as a tactical step in the short run, it doesn’t preclude us moving back to that sometime later if we decide that some of our options that we do pursue turn out to be less attractive for one reason or another.	92	9
201404	1704	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Yet if we adopt option 1 now, we may eviscerate the interbank lending markets, whether it be the federal funds market or other interbank lending markets, to the point that it would be hard to go back to them once we started targeting an administered rate.	92	9
201404	1705	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	It would be hard to go back to a market rate.	92	9
201404	1706	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think going with option 1 now does not preserve our options in an attractive way to me.	92	9
201404	1707	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I am concerned about some of the financial-stability issues that were raised about option 1 and the implications that facility might have.	92	9
201404	1708	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	During a period of financial stress, a run of investors in the market to this facility seems like a real possibility that could create serious funding issues for some borrowers.	92	9
201404	1709	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	More generally, I am not entirely convinced that the Federal Reserve should be the market’s primary supplier, maybe even its sole supplier, of risk-free overnight assets other than currency.	92	9
201404	1710	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	That is a big step, from supplying currency, to every other sort of risk-free asset that might be created.	92	9
201404	1711	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	And to make that argument simply on financial-stability grounds—that it makes it easier, as President Kocherlakota said, to do some things—I think we’d probably do those things anyway, and we’d figure out other ways to supply liquidity if we needed to.	92	9
201404	1712	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	The other thing that worries me a little bit in some of our discussions is some of the political risk, given the sizable expansion of our dealings with non-bank institutions that is required in these markets, such as money market mutual funds.	92	9
201404	1713	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I’d like to understand the consequences of that more broadly.	92	9
201404	1714	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I’m concerned about the implicit scale of these operations in a full-allotment system and the potential unintended consequences on the plumbing for the short- term money market.	92	9
201404	1715	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think there are just a lot of ramifications we probably don’t understand as of yet.	92	9
201404	1716	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I have similar concerns about option 2, which is a lot like option 1, except with a very narrow spread below the IOER rate.	92	9
201404	1717	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	So I kind of rule out option 2.	92	9
201404	1718	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	That leaves me with options 3, 4, and 5.	92	9
201404	1719	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Options 3 and 4 set an overnight rate of reverse repos far enough below the IOER rate to preserve the federal funds market or perhaps another interbank market of some kind.	92	9
201404	1720	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think that’s something reasonable to explore.	92	9
201404	1721	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Option 4 adds term deposits and term reverse repos.	92	9
201404	1722	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Option 5 relies on other term tools as well.	92	9
201404	1723	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I have to confess, I’m a little nervous with the term instruments.	92	9
201404	1724	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I would really prefer to stick with a market rate in overnight interbank markets or a reverse repo type-rate.	92	9
201404	1725	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Therefore, I have a little more attraction to options 3 and 4 than to 5.	92	9
201404	1726	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	As I said, I am open to redefining the federal funds rate or how we define the interbank market rate.	92	9
201404	1727	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I’m open to different ways of thinking about that, whether it be Eurodollars or some other construct.	92	9
201404	1728	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	But I’d like to know more about the types of traders in this market.	92	9
201404	1729	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	What’s the scale of it?	92	9
201404	1730	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	How much would we have to intervene?	92	9
201404	1731	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	What would the size of our balance sheet have to be in order to effectively function in that market?	92	9
201404	1732	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Can we identify trades by different types of traders?	92	9
201404	1733	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	The staff acknowledges that there are some legal ramifications here to redefining the fed funds rate.	92	9
201404	1734	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	We talked about those.	92	9
201404	1735	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think we can get over those in a reasonable manner.	92	9
201404	1736	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	The Federal Reserve and other regulators have raised serious concerns about money market mutual funds.	92	9
201404	1737	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	And yet, as we broaden our definition of the market rate or administered rate and the counterparties we have to deal with, we are beginning to rely on money market mutual funds as the primary transmission mechanism of monetary policy.	92	9
201404	1738	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Can we square our two views of regulation of money market mutual funds with using them as our primary transmission mechanism?	92	9
201404	1739	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I don’t know the answer to that, but I think it’s something we should give some thought.	92	9
201404	1740	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	More generally, I’d like to know more about the evolution of the Federal Reserve’s balance sheet under each of these options, in terms of its size and its composition in terms of short-term versus long-term assets that would be implied.	92	9
201404	1741	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	What would be the path of remittances?	92	9
201404	1742	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I do have concerns about the Federal Reserve’s exposure to interest rate risk under some of these options and what it entails for our remittances.	92	9
201404	1743	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	And I think we could be exposing ourselves to considerable political risk in this process.	92	9
201404	1744	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Indeed, I found all the memos a bit strange in that the reason we are engaged in this activity is that we have created a very large balance sheet.	92	9
201404	1745	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I mean, we did it, and so we are dealing with those issues, and in all of these memos we didn’t talk about what’s happening to the balance sheet and how it would be affected and how we want to manage that.	92	9
201404	1746	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think President Fisher alluded to this, and President Bullard alluded to this.	92	9
201404	1747	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Thinking about our short-term strategies, without thinking about how we are going to manage the balance sheet in the future, seems to be breaking this up in different pieces that may not be very productive.	92	9
201404	1748	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think we need to think about our balance sheet more.	92	9
201404	1749	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	We need to think about how we envision shrinking it.	92	9
201404	1750	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	And, by the way, as the balance sheet shrinks, the kind of problems we are dealing with become less of an issue.	92	9
201404	1751	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	So that is another way to deal with these issues.	92	9
201404	1752	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Regardless of which of these options are adopted, we need to start thinking about how to reduce the size of our balance sheet and how we can return it to a more normal size, sooner rather than later.	92	9
201404	1753	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Does that mean doing things like beginning to either slow or eliminate reinvestment policies?	92	9
201404	1754	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I suggested at an earlier meeting that, when we get to that stage, maybe one of the things we do is reinvest in short-term Treasuries rather than MBS and long-term Treasuries, as a way to create a more flexible structure of the balance sheet in terms of its composition, which might be helpful as well.	92	9
201404	1755	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	So we need to think about some of those things in conjunction with our operating framework.	92	9
201404	1756	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Finally, before I get to the quick answers to the questions, I am open to setting a range for the fed funds target.	92	9
201404	1757	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think in the near term—several people have mentioned this—we can stick with a range; the markets have kind of gotten used to that for the time being.	92	9
201404	1758	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Let’s experiment with how big the spread becomes as we raise the IOER rate.	92	9
201404	1759	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Do we need reverse RRPs to set a firmer floor under the lower part of that range?	92	9
201404	1760	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think those are interesting things that we can learn in the short term as we begin to move forward.	92	9
201404	1761	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	We may find that we don’t need to do it.	92	9
201404	1762	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Maybe the spread doesn’t widen as the IOER rate goes up.	92	9
201404	1763	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I don’t know the answer to that.	92	9
201404	1764	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	So I think those are things that are important to get a better handle on, and I think proceeding in that direction might be very, very helpful.	92	9
201404	1765	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I’ve answered most of the questions, but I’ll give a quick summary of the answers to the questions.	92	9
201404	1766	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	As to the fed funds market versus a more robust interbank market rate, I’m all for exploring different definitions of a robust interbank market rate as a market rate that we could target.	92	9
201404	1767	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think that’s something worth exploring.	92	9
201404	1768	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I am not in favor of going to the full-allotment overnight RRP facility at this point.	92	9
201404	1769	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think we can always revert to that later on, but once we revert to that it’s going to be very hard to move back to anything else.	92	9
201404	1770	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	And I think I still have just too many questions and concerns that.	92	9
201404	1771	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	The fourth question.	92	9
201404	1772	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	What’s the spread that is tolerable?	92	9
201404	1773	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I don’t have a real strong view about that.	92	9
201404	1774	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think that, as I pointed out earlier—and as I think President Lacker pointed out— what is really important for monetary policy is not what the size of that spread might be, but whether it is a useful signal for the path of monetary policy and whether other market rates are moving more or less in tandem with that.	92	9
201404	1775	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Regarding net interest expense issues and remittances, I think the stuff talked about in the memos are sort of peanuts compared with the fact that we’ve got this huge balance sheet.	92	9
201404	1776	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	We’ve got $3 trillion of reserves.	92	9
201404	1777	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	We get the IOER rate up to 200 basis points, and that’s $60 billion we are giving to banks, not giving to the US government in some accounting sense.	92	9
201404	1778	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Whether or not we are using an RRP facility versus the Term Deposit Facility is going to be peanuts compared with that number.	92	9
201404	1779	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	That is where our political risk arises, I think, not in the different methods we’re talking about here.	92	9
201404	1780	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	That’s really all about our balance sheet, and nothing in these memos really talks about that.	92	9
201404	1781	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I think we need to think more about the balance sheet.	92	9
201404	1782	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	With regard to further testing and the different spreads, I’m all fine for options 6 and 7, which is more testing.	92	9
201404	1783	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I do not want to go to the full-allotment test.	92	9
201404	1784	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	I don’t think that’s called for at this point; I think that’s something that we reserve.	92	9
201404	1785	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	If other things don’t work out, that’s something we may want to consider, but I wouldn’t want to go there yet.	92	9
201404	1786	2014-04-30	meeting	PLOSSER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
