201404	2190	2014-04-30	meeting		[Coffee break]	2	2
201404	2191	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Simon, do you want to begin the financial developments briefing?	61	6
201404	2192	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Okay.	61	6
201404	2193	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201404	2194	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Federal Reserve communications and economic data releases led market participants, on net, to expect an earlier liftoff and slightly higher target rate path.	61	6
201404	2195	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the top-left panel of your first exhibit, shorter-dated interest rates rose sharply following the March FOMC meeting, as market participants reacted to an unexpected increase in the SEP’s target rate values and to other policy communications.	61	6
201404	2196	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	While the March meeting minutes and some speeches over the period tempered this rise, shorter-dated rates ended the period moderately higher.	61	6
201404	2197	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	In contrast, the 10-year Treasury yield increased only modestly around the March meeting and moved in a very narrow range over the period.	61	6
201404	2198	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Expectations for a slightly earlier liftoff were also evident in the Desk’s dealer and buy-side surveys.	61	6
201404	2199	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the top-right panel, averaging across respondents’ probability assessments, each group now places higher odds on liftoff in 2015 and lower odds on liftoff in 2016 or later than they did at the time of the March survey.	61	6
201404	2200	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	In addition, the mean of expectations for the level of the target rate over the period from 2015 to 2017 shifted up a bit for both dealers and buy-side participants.	61	6
201404	2201	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	As I just noted, the 10-year Treasury yield has been moving in a very narrow range.	61	6
201404	2202	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	This stability against a backdrop of rising shorter-dated forward rates was the result of a similar-sized fall in longer-dated forward rates over the period, as shown in the middle-left panel.	61	6
201404	2203	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	The declines in the five-year, five-year forward nominal and real rates and rates further out on the curve continued a downward trend seen since the December FOMC meeting.	61	6
201404	2204	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Longer-dated nominal forward rates in other major developed economies have also declined notably since December, and have been highly correlated with corresponding US rates.	61	6
201404	2205	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	To better understand the moves in longer-dated forward rates in the United States, the Desk’s surveys asked respondents to decompose the roughly 75 basis point decline in the five-year, five-year forward nominal Treasury rate that occurred between the end of 2013 and mid-April into three components:  the expected average future real policy rate, expected future inflation, and term premium.	61	6
201404	2206	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the middle-right panel, buy-side participants generally cited lower expected average policy rates as accounting for the largest portion of the decline.	61	6
201404	2207	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	A change in the economic outlook, presumably for longer-run growth, was rated the most important factor driving this move on average.	61	6
201404	2208	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	The dealers, on average, attributed a greater portion of the decline to the term premium component, and placed a bit more weight on changes in perceptions of the Committee’s reaction function and “market-related factors” such as portfolio reallocation into fixed income at pension funds or safe- haven flows potentially stemming from tensions between Russia and Ukraine.	61	6
201404	2209	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Taken together, the survey responses suggest that a substantial part of the recent declines in forward rates may be due to reduced prospects for economic growth over the medium and longer term, consistent with recent market commentary on the declines in longer- dated forward rates.	61	6
201404	2210	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Alongside the declines in the five-year, five-year forward rates, the corresponding measure of interest rate implied volatility has declined in recent months and, as shown in the bottom-left panel, is back to levels seen just prior to the May 2013 JEC testimony.	61	6
201404	2211	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Other measures of implied volatility on longer-dated interest rates have also fallen.	61	6
201404	2212	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	In contrast, implied volatility on shorter-dated tenors has increased, which is consistent with the recent slight increase in the expected target rate path.	61	6
201404	2213	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Declines in broad measures of implied volatility have extended beyond US fixed-income and have also been seen in equity and currency markets, as shown in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201404	2214	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	All of these implied volatility measures are near their post- crisis lows, with broad fixed-income and currency measures near the lowest levels of their respective histories.	61	6
201404	2215	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	In explaining these low levels of implied volatility, market participants have pointed to a range of factors, including low realized volatility over recent months, greater certainty that the eventual normalization of US monetary policy will be gradual, and the belief that global monetary policies will remain accommodative well into the future.	61	6
201404	2216	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Some have also described increased confidence in a moderate growth outlook with limited inflation pressures.	61	6
201404	2217	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Finally, despite the ongoing tensions in Ukraine, others have noted lower so-called tail risks as contributing to the moves, including reduced fears of a euro-area breakup or a hard landing in China.	61	6
201404	2218	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Of course, in the past, periods of low volatility have at times been associated with an accumulation of financial imbalances and subsequent periods of higher volatility.	61	6
201404	2219	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Dan will provide an assessment of vulnerabilities in the financial system in his briefing.	61	6
201404	2220	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	The top-left panel of your next exhibit shows that the S&P 500 was little changed over the intermeeting period, though there were continued sharp declines in sectors that had previously outperformed the broader index, including the biotech and Internet sectors.	61	6
201404	2221	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Market participants did not cite a single catalyst for these declines but instead noted stretched valuations and overweight positioning among speculative investors as contributing factors.	61	6
201404	2222	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	US corporate credit continued its recent strong performance, as shown in the top-right panel.	61	6
201404	2223	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Market participants attributed the narrowing of investment-grade and high-yield spreads to an environment of subdued market volatility, low levels of actual and expected corporate defaults, and ongoing investor demand for higher- yielding fixed-income assets.	61	6
201404	2224	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Now, shifting abroad, market attention focused on official ECB commentary that discussed ways to address risks of low euro-area inflation for a prolonged period.	61	6
201404	2225	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	At the April ECB meeting, President Draghi noted that the Governing Council was “unanimous in its commitment” to utilize both unconventional and conventional instruments to combat the risks of persistently low inflation, including through quantitative easing.	61	6
201404	2226	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Thus far, this and other ECB commentary does not seem to have materially affected market-based measures of near-dated euro-area inflation compensation, shown in the middle-left panel.	61	6
201404	2227	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	These measures have been declining over the past year, particularly following the much lower-than-expected October euro-area inflation print.	61	6
201404	2228	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Evidence of increased expectations for further ECB easing is somewhat mixed across other euro-area financial markets.	61	6
201404	2229	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	While increased expectations for ECB asset purchases are consistent with the narrowing of peripheral euro-area sovereign spreads, shown in the middle-right panel, these spreads have been declining for some time amid a reach for yield by investors in a low volatility environment, as well as gradual improvement in the periphery fiscal and banking sector outlook.	61	6
201404	2230	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Partly reflecting these factors, Greece recently reentered international funding markets for the first time since 2010.	61	6
201404	2231	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Emerging market asset prices also increased over the period, as shown in the bottom-left panel.	61	6
201404	2232	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Market participants have noted increased demand for higher- yielding assets and attractive valuations as volatility has receded after the sharp price declines earlier this winter.	61	6
201404	2233	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Incoming economic information appears to explain little of the moves, given that economic growth was uneven across emerging markets and there was deterioration in the fundamentals of some countries whose markets outperformed, especially Brazil.	61	6
201404	2234	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Despite the recent abatement of market pressures, some market participants have cautioned that vulnerabilities remain elevated, heightening the need for broader reforms to reduce imbalances and lift growth prospects.	61	6
201404	2235	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Tensions between Russia and Ukraine remain an additional source of risk.	61	6
201404	2236	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Incoming economic data provided further evidence of a moderation in China’s growth trajectory, which Steve will discuss in greater detail in his briefing.	61	6
201404	2237	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Chinese policymakers responded to this first-quarter growth deceleration through a slight easing of policy.	61	6
201404	2238	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Over the period, Chinese money market rates remained below the average level of the past year and authorities lowered reserve requirements for rural commercial banks.	61	6
201404	2239	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	In addition, a new small-scale fiscal stimulus package was announced, although authorities downplayed the potential for any larger-scale action.	61	6
201404	2240	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	These statements were interpreted as underscoring Chinese policymakers’ intention to accept slightly lower economic growth without pursuing significant countercyclical measures.	61	6
201404	2241	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	The official Chinese exchange rate fixing continued to depreciate and both on- and off-shore renminbi traded at weaker levels in relation to the fixing, as shown in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201404	2242	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	It is unclear whether the continued depreciation has been driven by official sector intervention aimed at countering the moderation in Chinese growth, which would be consistent with other attempts to ease policy slightly, or if it reflects an abatement of external financial inflows and speculative positioning following increased currency volatility over recent months.	61	6
201404	2243	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Your final two exhibits review Desk operations.	61	6
201404	2244	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Our continued testing provided further evidence that the overnight RRP exercise is acting as a floor for overnight rates.	61	6
201404	2245	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	The past few weeks were a useful case study, as Treasury bill supply declined significantly because of seasonal patterns associated with federal tax receipts.	61	6
201404	2246	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	In past years, these declines in bill issuance have coincided with notable decreases in GC repo rates.	61	6
201404	2247	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the top-left panel, the recent decline in bill issuance is larger than it has been in recent years, yet overnight rates have been fairly stable so far, suggesting that the operations may be offsetting some of the downward pressure on market rates.	61	6
201404	2248	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Usage of the operations has picked up during the period of declining Treasury supply, as shown in the top-right panel.	61	6
201404	2249	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	High take-up tended to occur on days that GC repo traded at or below the overnight RRP rate, in line with the prior staff analysis showing that this take-up is sensitive to the spread between the operation fixed-rate and market rates.	61	6
201404	2250	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Usage was also heavy at the end of the first quarter, when take-up reached $242 billion.	61	6
201404	2251	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Despite the downward pressure on market rates from the decline in Treasury supply, in recent weeks more repo trades have occurred at or near the overnight RRP rate than earlier in the testing period, as shown in the middle-left panel.	61	6
201404	2252	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	However, we continue to see trades below the overnight RRP rate even for counterparties with access to the overnight RRP.	61	6
201404	2253	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Market participants suggest that one reason firms may choose to invest at a lower rate is to ensure continued access to dealer balance sheets.	61	6
201404	2254	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	On a related note, over the intermeeting period, the Federal Reserve System began receiving daily transaction data for federal funds, Eurodollar deposits, and CD markets as part of the FR 2420 data collection.	61	6
201404	2255	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	The data should help us better understand depository institutions’ unsecured funding activity and may be used to support calculation of the effective fed funds or new reference rates.	61	6
201404	2256	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Initial analysis of the FR 2420 data confirms that the majority of fed funds borrowing is done by foreign banking organizations at overnight tenors.	61	6
201404	2257	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Importantly, the FR 2420 data also provide a more complete sample of federal funds transactions than the brokered data that is currently used in the calculation of the effective fed funds rate.	61	6
201404	2258	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the middle-right panel, the effective fed funds rate broadly corresponds with the comparable fed funds rate calculated from FR 2420, and the daily distribution of rates across the two data sets is also similar.	61	6
201404	2259	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Average overnight Eurodollar rates derived from the new data set also generally correspond with rates received from brokers, although the volumes are notably lower as the FR 2420 data exclude many offshore entities that are active in this market.	61	6
201404	2260	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	The staff will continue to study the data and assess potential enhancements to the collection in the coming months.	61	6
201404	2261	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Next, I would like to mention a couple of recent developments in the MBS market.	61	6
201404	2262	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	First, option-adjusted spreads on current coupon MBS—shown in the bottom-left panel—have increased only slightly in recent months even as the pace of Federal Reserve asset purchases has declined, consistent with the view that MBS prices are affected by expectations for the total stock of purchases.	61	6
201404	2263	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	However, many market participants think that the daily rate of Federal Reserve purchases also affect MBS spreads.	61	6
201404	2264	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	They argue that spreads have remained stable amid declines in the pace of Fed purchases because gross issuance of MBS has continued to decline notably in response to higher mortgage rates since the middle of last year.	61	6
201404	2265	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the bottom-right panel, some of this decline in gross issuance is expected to reverse in coming months, largely because of seasonal factors, while market participants expect the Committee to continue decreasing the pace of MBS purchases.	61	6
201404	2266	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	As a result, the size of Federal Reserve purchases relative to the size of gross issuance is expected to decline significantly, and many market participants believe that spreads may widen some over the remainder of the year in response to this decline in our footprint.	61	6
201404	2267	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the bottom-right panel, under the Committee’s current policy regarding reinvestments, MBS purchases will likely remain large for some time.	61	6
201404	2268	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the top-left panel of your final exhibit, which pools responses across the recent dealer and buy-side surveys, respondents have varied views about the Committee’s likely future reinvestment policy.	61	6
201404	2269	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Dealers’ responses on the likely timing at which some or all reinvestments would end ranged from 9 months before liftoff to 12 months after liftoff, while buy-side views ranged from 9 months prior to liftoff to 30 months following liftoff.	61	6
201404	2270	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Given the projected size of reinvestments, the relative dispersion of views around the timing of any change in policy, and the importance that market participants place on those purchases, many are becoming increasingly focused on the Committee’s communication and intention on its balance sheet policy.	61	6
201404	2271	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Over the intermeeting period, the Desk began purchasing MBS on our proprietary FedTrade platform.	61	6
201404	2272	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	So far, the operations have gone well:  Systems are working as expected, pricing is competitive relative to market quotes, and dealer participation is strong, as reflected in the high offer-to-cover ratios shown in the top-right panel.	61	6
201404	2273	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	While large-scale auctions are not common in the MBS market and it is too soon to determine how the market will respond to a full transition to FedTrade, we are encouraged by the operations to date.	61	6
201404	2274	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	In Treasury markets, operations continue to proceed smoothly and are well- subscribed.	61	6
201404	2275	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	If the Committee chooses to decrease the pace of Treasury purchases at this meeting, the Desk will conduct fewer operations each month, while leaving the maturity distribution of purchases unchanged.	61	6
201404	2276	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	If purchases are reduced, we would release a Desk statement at the same time as the Committee statement, the same approach as taken at prior meetings.	61	6
201404	2277	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Lorie and I will have copies of the statement available for review tomorrow.	61	6
201404	2278	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Finally, as explained in the memo that Steve Kamin and I sent to the Committee on April 22, we are requesting votes to renew the liquidity swap lines and NAFA arrangements.	61	6
201404	2279	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the middle-left panel, the use of liquidity swap lines recently has been minimal, and as communicated in a memo earlier this year, the foreign central banks plan to phase out their auctions of dollar liquidity by the end of July.	61	6
201404	2280	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Even though planned dollar operations could end soon, we believe that the standing arrangements are an important liquidity backstop, helping to maintain stability and confidence in global funding markets.	61	6
201404	2281	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Additionally, liquidity swap and NAFA arrangements are tangible and constructive signals of central bank cooperation.	61	6
201404	2282	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201404	2283	2014-04-30	meeting	POTTER	That completes my prepared remarks.	61	6

201404	2387	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	The data on real activity and inflation that we have received since the March Tealbook contained relatively little in the way of material surprises, and thus we made only small revisions to our economic projections in the April Tealbook.	11	1
201404	2388	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	As you can see from the top two panels of your forecast summary exhibit, the incoming spending data resulted in an upward revision to fourth-quarter real GDP growth and a downward revision to the first quarter.	11	1
201404	2389	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	The fourth-quarter surprise was concentrated in consumption services, while the first- quarter surprise was mostly attributable to an unexpected decline in exports.	11	1
201404	2390	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	I would note as an aside that given how low our point estimate now is for first-quarter growth—and taking account of the sizable error band that surrounds even a forecast on the eve of release—it would not be particularly unusual from a statistical point of view if tomorrow’s advance estimate were to show a small decline in first-quarter real GDP.	11	1
201404	2391	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	Despite the downward revision to our Q1 estimate, we continue to think that GDP was held down last quarter by several transitory factors, including unusually severe winter weather and the aforementioned decline in exports.	11	1
201404	2392	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	Hence, we continue to anticipate that real GDP growth will step up to a 3½ percent pace this quarter.	11	1
201404	2393	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	Much of the higher-frequency data that we received during the intermeeting period seems consistent with this near-term picture.	11	1
201404	2394	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	In particular, both retail sales and motor vehicle sales picked up sharply in March.	11	1
201404	2395	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	Likewise, after a sharp decline in January that was largely weather induced, manufacturing production rebounded in February and rose further in March.	11	1
201404	2396	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	And, after the Tealbook was closed, we received the advance report on durable goods, which showed increases in orders and shipments of nondefense capital goods last month that are broadly consistent with the modest step-up in business investment we are projecting this quarter.	11	1
201404	2397	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	One component of demand that has fallen short of our expectations is residential construction.	11	1
201404	2398	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	Specifically, single-family starts last month were softer than we had projected in the March Tealbook; building permit issuance, which we generally view as a better indicator of the underlying pace of construction, also surprised us to the downside and remains noticeably below the levels seen last year.	11	1
201404	2399	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	It is possible that bad weather depressed starts and permits in the early part of the year to a greater degree than we had anticipated.	11	1
201404	2400	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	Nevertheless, as shown in the middle-left panel, we took some signal from the incoming data and marked down our forecast for residential investment growth in the first half and, to a lesser extent, for the year as a whole.	11	1
201404	2401	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	Our view that there might be more underlying weakness in the housing sector than we had previously thought was reinforced by the softer-than-expected data on March home sales, though here too our uncertainty regarding the effects of bad weather—and the usual month-to-month volatility of some of these measures—make us hesitant to mark down our outlook too drastically at this point.	11	1
201404	2402	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	Moreover, given the continued rise in house prices, it seems likely that at least some of the slow pace of sales and construction reflects supply constraints, a hypothesis supported by evidence of rising input costs as well as anecdotes from builders.	11	1
201404	2403	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	Taking a broader view, however, we still see the fundamentals for the housing sector as favorable, and thus we continue to project a noticeable acceleration in residential construction as the effects of bad weather unwind, the overall economy improves, and as supply-related constraints gradually diminish.	11	1
201404	2404	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	But we admit to being somewhat nervous about that projection.	11	1
201404	2405	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	Turning to the labor market, the March employment report came in about as expected.	11	1
201404	2406	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	On the establishment side, the average pace of job gains for the first quarter as a whole was in line with our March projection, and we continue to anticipate a modest rise in job growth over the near term.	11	1
201404	2407	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	On the household side, the March unemployment rate was one-tenth higher than we had expected, while the labor force participation rate was 0.2 percentage point higher.	11	1
201404	2408	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	For the near term, we have taken on board the small upward surprise to the unemployment rate but are inclined to attribute some of last month’s improvement in the participation rate to noise.	11	1
201404	2409	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	Combined, these revisions leave our current assessment of labor market slack about unrevised, with an employment-to-population ratio that is in line with our previous forecast.	11	1
201404	2410	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	Our medium-term GDP projection is also little changed from March:  As noted, the incoming data seem consistent with our view that the weakness seen in the first quarter was mostly transitory, and we made only small and offsetting revisions to our conditioning factors this round.	11	1
201404	2411	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	We therefore continue to project that real GDP growth will pick up to an average pace that is just above 3 percent per year as some of the forces that have been restraining growth in recent years—such as federal fiscal policy—start to fade.	11	1
201404	2412	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	With a rate of potential output growth that is expected to average a touch below 2 percent over the next few years, this pace of actual output growth implies a steady reduction in the unemployment rate, to just over 5 percent at the end of 2016.	11	1
201404	2413	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	This path is basically identical to our previous forecast and leaves the unemployment rate at our estimate of its natural rate at the end of the projection period.	11	1

201404	2419	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	With projected slack, inflation expectations, and core import prices all little revised relative to March, we made no change to our core inflation forecast; likewise, our projection for headline inflation is basically unrevised after this year.	11	1
201404	2420	2014-04-30	meeting	WASCHER	In particular, we continue to expect a gradual rise in core inflation over the medium term as margins of labor- and product-market slack tighten further, as some of the transitory factors that depressed inflation in 2013 are not repeated, and as core import prices return to a moderate rate of increase following their decline last year.	11	1

201404	2423	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	I will not be referring to a handout.	11	1
201404	2424	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Like many cars driving on Washington roads following our unusually harsh winter, the foreign economy ran into a pothole early this year.	11	1
201404	2425	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	After averaging 3 percent in the second half of last year, foreign growth slowed to only 2¼ percent in the first quarter, ½ percentage point below what we wrote down in March.	11	1
201404	2426	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Much of the slowdown was concentrated in China and its emerging market neighbors, and importantly reflected a drop-off in exports.	11	1
201404	2427	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	As I’ll discuss shortly, our best guess is that Chinese growth will regain some of its earlier momentum in the next few quarters, while Latin America’s economy, which has also languished of late, will pick up too.	11	1
201404	2428	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Accordingly, we see foreign growth clambering out of the pothole with its hubcaps still on, reaching 3¼ percent by the second half of this year and maintaining that pace for the remainder of the forecast period.	11	1
201404	2429	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Notably, as Bill discussed, the US economy also hit a pothole in the first quarter, in part reflecting the same factor restraining many foreign economies:  contracting trade.	11	1
201404	2430	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	The contribution of net exports to US GDP swung from positive 1 percentage point in the fourth quarter to an estimated negative 1 percentage point in the first, as exports plunged at a 5½ percent rate.	11	1
201404	2431	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Because the export decline chiefly reflected contracting shipments of oil and agricultural products, which had enjoyed outsized gains the quarter before, we are inclined to view it as transitory and project exports to resume growing in the current quarter, erasing the drag on US GDP.	11	1
201404	2432	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	By the same token, the export slowdown in the EMEs, which included a step-down in shipments of high-tech goods, also follows a strong fourth quarter.	11	1
201404	2433	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	This gives us some optimism that trade and economic activity will also pick up in the EMEs, supporting global growth.	11	1
201404	2434	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	However, this outlook for renewed global growth is hardly assured, and China represents the biggest question mark.	11	1
201404	2435	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Based on the GDP data released by the Chinese authorities, we estimate that the pace of expansion dropped from 8 percent in the fourth quarter to only 5½ percent in the first.	11	1
201404	2436	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Industrial production, investment, and exports all weakened significantly.	11	1
201404	2437	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	The causes of the slowdown are murky.	11	1
201404	2438	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Over the past year or so, the authorities had taken actions to rein in credit growth, boost interest rates, and generally rebalance the economy away from investment and exports, and we were expecting some moderation in growth, but nothing this abrupt.	11	1
201404	2439	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Moreover, China’s exports appear to have fallen considerably further than those of most other Asian economies, raising questions as to whether some of the reported decline may be due to statistical problems.	11	1
201404	2440	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	All told, our best guess is that at least some of the slowdown was due to transitory factors and Chinese economic growth will move back up to over 7 percent in the second half of this year as exports strengthen and domestic policy turns more supportive.	11	1
201404	2441	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	To be sure, China’s authorities have been quite outspoken that they are not planning substantial additional stimulus, but they will probably either deliver that stimulus or at least ease off their earlier tightening if economic growth continues to perform much below their current 7½ percent target.	11	1
201404	2442	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	As Chinese growth recovers, it should support a more rapid expansion in other EMEs, especially in Asia, that have also underperformed recently.	11	1
201404	2443	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	This outlook is reasonably benign, and in putting it together, we considered whether we might be seeing the beginnings of a financial crisis in China, with shortfalls in activity eventually triggering sharp downdrafts in property and financial markets.	11	1
201404	2444	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Notwithstanding some isolated corporate defaults and a localized run on a rural bank, however, we’ve seen scant evidence of more generalized disruptions, and we continue to view a significant surge in financial volatility as a downside risk rather than a feature of our baseline outlook.	11	1
201404	2445	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Two other risks bear mention.	11	1
201404	2446	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	First, the situation in Ukraine is deteriorating, and as noted in the Tealbook, a substantial escalation of geopolitical tensions could boost oil prices, depress sentiment, and weigh on US and global growth.	11	1
201404	2447	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Second, as Simon discussed earlier, although financial stresses in EMEs eased further since your last meeting, some EMEs continue to harbor significant vulnerabilities, and a renewal of stresses, perhaps as we and other major central banks start to raise rates, remains a possibility.	11	1
201404	2448	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Assuming these risks do not materialize, our outlook for the advanced foreign economies is also reasonably benign, though hardly ebullient, with economic growth averaging 2¼ percent over the forecast period.	11	1
201404	2449	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	This is a little higher than their estimated potential growth, so resource slack diminishes over time.	11	1
201404	2450	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Economic indicators in the euro area have been reasonably upbeat, and growth looks set to edge up over the forecast period—reaching 2 percent by 2016—on the back of further reductions in financial stresses and fiscal drag.	11	1
201404	2451	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	The Japanese economy will likely contract this quarter as a result of the hike in consumption taxes on April 1, but some offsetting government spending and continued asset purchases should support above- trend growth, on average, even given a second tax hike scheduled for the end of next year.	11	1
201404	2452	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Perhaps reflecting some lack of imagination on our part, by the end of the forecast period, we see the situation in the advanced foreign economies as broadly similar to that in the United States, with output close to its potential level, inflation approaching the 2 percent target, and policy interest rates still well below their likely long-run levels.	11	1
201404	2453	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Although continued monetary policy accommodation abroad seems nearly assured, policy rate paths will likely diverge considerably across the major central banks.	11	1
201404	2454	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	In the United Kingdom, continued brisk GDP growth along with continued weak productivity pushed the unemployment rate down to 6.9 percent, below the 7 percent threshold announced last August.	11	1
201404	2455	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	The Bank of England is expected to start raising its policy rate in the first quarter of 2015, even before the staff’s projection has the FOMC starting to tighten.	11	1
201404	2456	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	At the other end of the spectrum, we see the Bank of Japan continuing its heavy asset purchases through the end of 2015, a year later than specified in the BOJ’s initial announcement of its program last year.	11	1
201404	2457	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	That said, we’ve abandoned our earlier assumption that the BOJ will substantially step up the pace of its purchases, as BOJ officials have signaled greater comfort with the progress of inflation and output, despite the fact that both of them have come in weaker than we’d expected recently.	11	1
201404	2458	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Prospects for monetary policy are especially uncertain in the euro area.	11	1
201404	2459	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	The ECB continues to grapple with whether or not to provide additional stimulus.	11	1
201404	2460	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Although the economy is now in its fifth quarter of recovery, unemployment remains stuck near 12 percent, and 12-month headline inflation has continued to decline recently, falling to 0.5 percent in March.	11	1
201404	2461	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	As Simon noted, ECB officials have signaled their interest in various options—ranging from providing further liquidity to lowering interest rates, all the way to purchases of asset-backed securities or government bonds—depending on whether and to what extent the risks of disinflation become more pronounced.	11	1
201404	2462	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	However, beyond relatively modest actions such as providing additional LTROs, more-aggressive measures would all have their drawbacks.	11	1
201404	2463	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Accordingly, we do not see the ECB starting asset purchases unless a significant deterioration of the outlook forces its hand.	11	1
201404	2464	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	At this point, that seems unlikely.	11	1
201404	2465	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Much of the euro area’s recent disinflation has been driven by falling retail energy prices, while core inflation has run higher at almost 1 percent.	11	1
201404	2466	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	For the period ahead, we anticipate that a bottoming out of energy prices and narrowing of output gaps will push inflation up to 1½ percent toward the end of next year, hardly rapid progress, but enough to keep the ECB on hold until 2016, when we expect it to start raising rates.	11	1
201404	2467	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	That concludes my prepared remarks.	11	1
201404	2468	2014-04-30	meeting	KAMIN	Dan Covitz will now continue our presentation.	11	1
201404	2469	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	I’ll be referring to the three exhibits with the cover page entitled, “Material for Financial Stability Assessment.”	11	1
201404	2470	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	My briefing is based on our recent QS Assessment of Financial Stability.	11	1
201404	2471	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	As in previous reports, we focus on vulnerabilities, where vulnerabilities are aspects of the financial system that could amplify shocks and in doing so impose negative externalities, such as fire sales and other forms of contagion, on the financial system.	11	1
201404	2472	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Our bottom line is that, overall, vulnerabilities remain moderate, although some appear to be expanding relative to the December assessment.	11	1
201404	2473	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Our overall assessment is predicated, in part, on the aggregate level of maturity transformation we see in the financial system, which appears low relative to pre-crisis levels.	11	1
201404	2474	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	As shown in panel 1 of your first exhibit, the ratio of net short-term wholesale funding to gross domestic product has remained at the lower end of its range over the past several years, reflecting, in part, a reduction in total triparty repurchase agreements (not shown).	11	1
201404	2475	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	In addition, as illustrated in panel 2, the level of triparty repurchase agreements backed by relatively illiquid collateral, the area above the dark blue region, has changed little over the past several quarters.	11	1
201404	2476	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Moreover, the flow of assets being securitized, charted in panel 3, has picked up only a bit from moribund levels in 2008, driven primarily by increases in CMBS and CLOs.	11	1
201404	2477	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Securitization was the first step in large volumes of maturity transformation chains in the shadow banking system that proved unstable during the financial crisis.	11	1
201404	2478	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	In addition, leverage in the financial sector appears relatively low.	11	1
201404	2479	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Panel 4 shows that regulatory capital ratios at bank holding companies are at their highest levels in over a decade.	11	1
201404	2480	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	In addition, as outlined in panel 5, all of the domestic systemically important banking firms (G-SIBs) reported they had met their minimum required Basel III Tier I Capital Ratios, including the firm-specific G-SIB surcharge.	11	1
201404	2481	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Further, the Federal Reserve’s Dodd-Frank stress tests showed that all of the 30 largest bank holding companies were projected to exceed their minimum capital requirements under the adverse scenario, which included a large interest rate shock, and all but one of the 30 largest bank holding companies was projected to exceed their minimum capital requirements under the severely adverse economic scenario.	11	1
201404	2482	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Moreover, as shown in panel 6, dealer responses to the most recent Senior Credit Officer Opinion Survey indicate the use of leverage at REITs has declined in recent quarters, while the use of leverage at hedge funds has moved sideways, although staff estimates of hedge fund leverage indicate that such leverage is high relative to its range over the past couple of years.	11	1
201404	2483	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Finally, rapidly expanding credit in the nonfinancial sector (not shown)—a typical precursor to financial instability—has been limited.	11	1
201404	2484	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Household borrowing has been held down, in part by uncertainties about risks to making mortgages in the current regulatory environment and the ongoing effects of lending restrictions in the Credit Card Act.	11	1
201404	2485	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Debt growth of the nonfinancial business sector has been robust, but many firms have continued to take advantage of low rates to refinance existing debt and reduce their interest expenses.	11	1
201404	2486	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Now the bad news:  As discussed in your next exhibit, pockets of vulnerabilities have persisted and in some cases appear to be expanding.	11	1
201404	2487	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Beginning with panel 7, valuation ratios—that is, forward P/E ratios—of small capitalization stocks, the red line, remain high by historical standards, notwithstanding the recent sizable correction in biotech and social media stocks.	11	1
201404	2488	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	In addition, margin credit on equity investments has increased notably relative to market capitalization.	11	1
201404	2489	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Even so, valuation ratios for larger firms, the black line, continue to appear moderate.	11	1
201404	2490	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Moreover, staff measures of the equity risk premium for S&P 500 firms are still wide by historical standards and so do not suggest, broadly speaking, that the stock market is overvalued.	11	1
201404	2491	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	For Treasury securities, valuation pressures remain evident to some degree.	11	1
201404	2492	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	As plotted in panel 8, staff estimates of the term premium on 10-year nominal Treasury securities are at the lower end of their historical range, despite the jump last summer, suggesting that term premiums could move up further.	11	1
201404	2493	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Elsewhere in the fixed- income sector, spreads on corporate bonds have continued to decline, with the high- yield spread, the black line in panel 9, moving toward the bottom of its historical range.	11	1
201404	2494	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Nevertheless, the low level of spreads suggests that potential exists for the price of credit risk to rise; indeed, historically narrow corporate bond spreads are empirically associated with subsequent mark-to-market losses on corporate bonds.	11	1
201404	2495	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	In the leveraged loan market, excesses have continued to build since the December QS assessment.	11	1
201404	2496	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	As indicated by the combined height of the bars in panel 10, the pace of leveraged loan issuance increased further this year, surpassing the pace in each of the past 10 years.	11	1
201404	2497	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Moreover, most of the increase is attributed to deals with debt exceeding six times EBITDA, the blue bars.	11	1
201404	2498	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	In addition, spreads have remained narrow and covenants have reportedly weakened further.	11	1
201404	2499	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Of course, the pressures in the leveraged loan market are not new.	11	1
201404	2500	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Supervisory guidance was issued early last year, followed by letters pointing to Matters Requiring Attention (MRAs) in the fall, to address the evident deterioration in banks’ leveraged loan underwriting practices.	11	1
201404	2501	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	However, we have yet to see a noticeable effect of the guidance or the MRAs on loan volumes, credit terms, or deal structures.	11	1
201404	2502	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	We will know more about the efficacy of the guidance after this summer’s SNC exams.	11	1
201404	2503	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	However, even if the MRAs succeed in curtailing unsound practices at banks, leveraged lending activity could migrate to nonbank lenders such as private equity firms and hedge funds— indeed, some deals reportedly have been done recently without bank participation.	11	1
201404	2504	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	A related vulnerability is the liquidity risk posed by the rapid growth in business debt held by mutual funds over the past few years.	11	1
201404	2505	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	As illustrated in panel 11, outstanding assets under management at mutual funds totaled roughly $2½ trillion in 2013.	11	1
201404	2506	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	These funds offer daily liquidity to investors, even though most of the underlying assets are fairly illiquid.	11	1
201404	2507	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	To be sure, bid-asked spreads (not shown) on corporate bonds are not high right now.	11	1
201404	2508	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	However, the role of dealers in providing liquidity to corporate debt markets has diminished.	11	1
201404	2509	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	As shown by the black line in panel 12, the ratio of outstanding corporate debt to dealer holdings, at over 12, is near its highest level in several years, as dealers are reportedly moving toward intermediating trades only when they already have a buyer and a seller lined up.	11	1
201404	2510	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Your final exhibit summarizes an alternative simulation in the April Tealbook, Book A, entitled “Liftoff Tantrum,” which uses the FRB/US model to capture the potential economic effects from triggering some of the pressures that I just highlighted.	11	1
201404	2511	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	In that simulation, term premiums are assumed to rise by 120 basis points more than expected over the first half of 2015, and investment-grade corporate bond spreads widen by 70 basis points.	11	1
201404	2512	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	The triggering event is presumed to be a pull- forward by investors of the eventual tightening of conventional monetary policy and the depressing effects on the market values of fixed-income portfolios.	11	1
201404	2513	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	In this scenario, the effect on the unemployment rate peaks at 0.3 percentage point in 2016 and moderates to about 0.2 percentage point by 2018, while the effect on the level of GDP peaks at 80 basis points and also ebbs a bit through 2018.	11	1
201404	2514	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	In the simulation, households and investors anticipate that the turmoil, while intense, will be transitory, which limits the effects on permanent income.	11	1
201404	2515	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	In addition, there is a modest policy offset.	11	1
201404	2516	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	However, it is not unimaginable that the pockets of vulnerabilities in high-yield debt markets could be more disruptive than in the simulation.	11	1
201404	2517	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	For instance, negative returns on high-yield bonds could cause dealers to pull back, and, as a result, the broader corporate bond market could become highly illiquid, perhaps disrupting the primary issuance market as well.	11	1
201404	2518	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Such an event would be more consequential for the real economy, although effects would be mitigated by moderate leverage in both the financial and nonfinancial sectors, and by the subdued amounts of assets funded with short-term debt relative to levels leading up to the financial crisis.	11	1
201404	2519	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	I’ll conclude by noting that while financial vulnerabilities remain modest overall, we cannot rule out the possibility that the financial system would become impaired from a large and adverse shock, such as a resurgence of instability in Europe, or a marked deterioration of the situation in Ukraine.	11	1
201404	2520	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	Thank you, Madam Chair.	11	1
201404	2521	2014-04-30	meeting	COVITZ	That concludes our prepared remarks.	11	1

201404	2821	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Why don’t we begin the economic go-round and start with President Williams?	13	1
201404	2822	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201404	2823	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The ongoing recovery appears to be back on track, with the severe winter weather that was talked so much about and the accompanying hiccup in economic growth now behind us.	13	1
201404	2824	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	So, like the Tealbook, I have not materially changed my projections for growth or inflation from what I wrote down at our last meeting.	13	1
201404	2825	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In fact, in the “Forecast Summary,”	13	1
201404	2826	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I was struck by how nearly identical the forecast lines for March and April are for unemployment, GDP growth, and inflation.	13	1
201404	2827	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In March, consumer and business spending posted solid gains, and my business contacts are generally optimistic about the rest of the year.	13	1
201404	2828	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Even in real estate, which hasn’t yet rebounded from the winter slump, the mood in my part of the country is decidedly upbeat.	13	1
201404	2829	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	A member of our Economic Advisory Council says the San Francisco real estate market is the strongest he’s seen in his entire life.	13	1
201404	2830	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, right after he said that, another member of the council asked, “But is it a bubble?”	13	1
201404	2831	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	He responded, without even pausing, “Of course.”	13	1
201404	2832	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	[Laughter]	13	1
201404	2833	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	And a contact in door and window manufacturing is very bullish about remodeling and homebuilding nationwide.	13	1
201404	2834	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In terms of labor market conditions, a wide range of indicators continue to improve.	13	1
201404	2835	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Payroll and household employment have both shown solid gains, and the unemployment rate, though still high, has fallen briskly over the past year.	13	1
201404	2836	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	One important labor market indicator that has yet to show signs of life is wages.	13	1
201404	2837	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	I will spend the rest of my time—I’ll just spend the rest of the afternoon [laughter]—discussing why the muted wage growth we’ve seen so far is consistent with a strengthening labor market.	13	1
201404	2838	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In a healthy economy, with inflation near our target, broad measures of nominal compensation—wages, salaries, and benefits—should be rising about 3½ to 4 percent per year to keep up with inflation and productivity growth.	13	1
201404	2839	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In contrast, for the past three years, we’ve seen an increase in compensation that has fallen well short of that pace, with most measures centering around 2 percent.	13	1
201404	2840	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Average hourly earnings is one indicator that hints at a desirable acceleration in wages.	13	1
201404	2841	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Even there, the rate of increase is still well below normal levels.	13	1
201404	2842	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, the slow recovery in wages is confirmed by my contacts.	13	1
201404	2843	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	They report limited pressures to boost compensation, except in a few selected hot markets.	13	1
201404	2844	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	And they expect wage increases to remain modest in the coming year.	13	1
201404	2845	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	How should we interpret the muted pace of wage growth?	13	1
201404	2846	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Namely, is it a sign that the improvement in the labor market may have been more modest than these other indicators suggest?	13	1
201404	2847	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	My staff looked into this question and found that the current pattern of relatively weak wage growth during the early and middle parts of a recovery is not actually unique.	13	1
201404	2848	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In fact, the recoveries in the early 1990s and early 2000s displayed a similar pattern, in which wages lagged the cycle.	13	1
201404	2849	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In those episodes, unemployment gaps, though never as large as in the current episode, narrowed significantly before the pace of wage increases picked up from low levels.	13	1
201404	2850	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	To explain why a pickup in wage growth lags a strengthening labor market, research by my staff emphasizes that wages don’t adjust as quickly as we might think.	13	1
201404	2851	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In particular, they find that nominal wage cuts are very rare.	13	1
201404	2852	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	This downward nominal wage rigidity turns out to imply that wage growth remains low until the recovery is pretty well advanced.	13	1
201404	2853	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The constraint on wage cuts was particularly binding after the Great Recession, due to the severity of the economic shocks, along with low inflation.	13	1
201404	2854	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	As a result, a very high share of workers reported that they earned the same wage as they had earned a year earlier.	13	1
201404	2855	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Early in the recovery, the share of workers with essentially unchanged wages reached the highest level since the day the series began in 1980, nearing 17 percent in 2011.	13	1
201404	2856	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	That compares with about 11 percent in 2007.	13	1
201404	2857	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	This pattern of a rising share of workers with unchanged wages was also seen in the recoveries of the early 1990s and 2000s.	13	1
201404	2858	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Earlier studies—including those by James Tobin, George Akerlof, and others— highlighted the importance of downward nominal wage rigidities.	13	1
201404	2859	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	My staff extended this research to study the response to recessionary shocks.	13	1
201404	2860	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In their DSGE model, many workers should see wage cuts in a downturn but do not, because of the zero lower bound on wage adjustments.	13	1
201404	2861	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	That means that wage growth falls by less during the recession than it would otherwise, and, as a result, once the economy starts to recover, a stock-up of pent-up wage cuts needs to be overcome before the pace of wage increases can return to normal.	13	1
201404	2862	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	This occurs only slowly as inflation and productivity growth bring real wages back into balance.	13	1
201404	2863	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	The key takeaway is that muted wage growth, both in this model and based on historical experience, is entirely consistent with an improving labor market in a low-inflation environment.	13	1
201404	2864	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	In the model, wage growth lags the cycle and picks up only as we get closer to full employment.	13	1
201404	2865	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Again, this theoretical result matches what we saw in the 1990s and 2000s, two other periods in which downward nominal wage rigidity appeared to be binding for many workers.	13	1
201404	2866	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Finally, as we close in on full employment over the next year or two, a return to more normal patterns of wage growth should reemerge.	13	1
201404	2867	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Indeed, we are seeing incipient signs of this normalization in the wage process, with the share of workers experiencing zero wage adjustments having already started to come down, albeit only slightly.	13	1
201404	2868	2014-04-30	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you.	13	1
201404	2869	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1
201404	2870	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	13	1
201404	2871	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201404	2872	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	The first quarter looks to be a disappointment, with real GDP growing close to 1 percent, much lower than what we’d expected at the time of the December FOMC meeting.	13	1
201404	2873	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Despite the setback, the economy does again seem poised to grow above potential over the course of this year.	13	1
201404	2874	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	My own forecast is for real GDP growth over the next three quarters to be around 3 percent, a little slower than the Tealbook forecast.	13	1
201404	2875	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	One of the key issues in the forecast is the path of the labor force participation rate.	13	1
201404	2876	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	About half of the decline in labor force participation since the onset of the Great Recession is a result of an aging population.	13	1
201404	2877	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	There is an ongoing debate about how much of the other half of the decline—which reflects declines in participation rates within specific age cohorts, including prime-age working cohorts—is bound to be reversed as labor market conditions improve further.	13	1
201404	2878	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Work done by the Boston staff has looked at the Panel Study of Income Dynamics, or PSID, which provides longitudinal data on individuals’ work history.	13	1
201404	2879	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	These data can be used to analyze the behavior of individuals who drop out of the labor force during stressful economic times—in particular, whether they’ve later been successful reentering the labor force.	13	1
201404	2880	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	The study pooled individuals not in the labor force during the previous recessions and recoveries who had previously worked to try to better understand the extent of reentry by age group.	13	1
201404	2881	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	The results indicate that 78 percent of the individuals between the ages of 25 and 44 who left the labor force during periods of economic stress were working again within four years.	13	1
201404	2882	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	This drops to 40 percent for individuals in the 45-to-54 age cohort who exit the labor force during periods of economic stress.	13	1
201404	2883	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	This indicates that roughly two-thirds of individuals in the 25-to-54 age cohort who historically left the workforce during the stressful economic period later reentered the workforce.	13	1
201404	2884	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Note that there are differences across time periods, and this period could be different than the historical average.	13	1
201404	2885	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, during periods of tight labor markets, such as the late 1990s, the data show significant reentry, even by workers who had previously left the labor force by retiring.	13	1
201404	2886	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	This research highlights that labor force participation is likely to improve as labor markets tighten, as past experience suggests that a substantial portion of the decline in labor force participation within age-specific cohorts during a recession and the early stages of a recovery is temporary.	13	1
201404	2887	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Both my somewhat slower real GDP growth projection compared with the Tealbook and my expectation that there is likely to be reentry into the labor force as labor markets tighten make me somewhat less optimistic than the Tealbook about how quickly we will reach full employment.	13	1
201404	2888	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	With PCE inflation well below our target and many advanced economies also experiencing unusually low inflation rates, we should be particularly attentive to whether incoming data are consistent with our inflation forecast.	13	1
201404	2889	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Low inflation and unusually low compensation growth give us the flexibility to try to more quickly normalize labor markets.	13	1
201404	2890	2014-04-30	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201404	2953	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Based on March data and these anecdotal reports, I’m holding to an outlook of medium- term real GDP growth around 3 percent.	13	1
201404	2954	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	This is the same outlook I presented at the last meeting.	13	1
201404	2955	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	I’m expecting this growth to be sufficient to keep net monthly job gains in the neighborhood of 200,000, even as productivity growth improves.	13	1
201404	2956	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	My outlook projects unemployment reaching 5¼ percent by the end of 2016 and inflation converging to our 2 percent objective about the same time.	13	1
201404	2957	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	With this baseline scenario, I have liftoff for the fed funds rate occurring late in 2015, followed by a gradual process of normalization of the policy rate.	13	1
201404	2958	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	In its essentials, my outlook doesn’t deviate significantly from that of this meeting’s Tealbook.	13	1
201404	2959	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	My staff has proposed to me a monitoring and validation framework with a number of indicators but three bellwethers in particular:  industrial production growth, demand for capital goods, and consumer spending.	13	1
201404	2960	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Interestingly, we saw improvement in all of these categories in the March data.	13	1
201404	2961	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	The main point I want to make in this round is that it will likely be very challenging over the coming months to see clear validation in the data of an assumed outlook of 3 percent economic growth.	13	1
201404	2962	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	We may not know for several quarters whether the economy is on a stronger sustained growth path.	13	1
201404	2963	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Given normal monthly variability of readings, distinguishing between a 3 percent and a 2 percent growth path may take a while.	13	1
201404	2964	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Certainly, there are risks around my outlook that are well captured by the range of alternative scenarios presented in the Tealbook.	13	1
201404	2965	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	The one I find most plausible is the “Weaker Household Demand” scenario.	13	1
201404	2966	2014-04-30	meeting	LOCKHART	Because of the murkiness we may be dealing with as the data come in, I would counsel caution about projecting a funds rate liftoff too early and running risks in the Committee’s communication of the market pulling forward the date.	13	1

201404	2990	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	I think the intermeeting reports haven’t been really informative enough to alter the outlook, so I’m still forecasting fairly tepid growth.	13	1
201404	2991	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	I’ll join my colleagues from the 1st and 12th Districts by providing a research report on labor markets.	13	1
201404	2992	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	We’ve often discussed whether the unemployment rate is a reliable measure of resource underutilization.	13	1
201404	2993	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	I want to talk about—this is something I mentioned last time—a generalized index of labor underutilization that our folks have constructed.	13	1
201404	2994	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	The project starts from the premise that there’s substantial underutilization beyond what’s captured in the standard unemployment rate.	13	1
201404	2995	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	That’s motivated by the significant flows you see from out of the labor force directly to employment rather than spending time in unemployment.	13	1
201404	2996	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	There are a lot of differences across nonemployed workers in the rate at which they transition to employment.	13	1
201404	2997	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	The index is essentially a weighted average of everybody who’s not employed full time, but the weights have to do with the rate of transition to full-time work.	13	1
201404	2998	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	And the differences are pretty significant.	13	1
201404	2999	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	Here’s an interesting observation:  The short-term unemployed, those unemployed less than 26 weeks, have the highest probability of transitioning to full-time employment.	13	1
201404	3000	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	It’s about 0.3.	13	1
201404	3001	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	For the long-term unemployed, the probability of transitioning to full-time work is roughly half that—about 0.15.	13	1
201404	3002	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	The striking feature of the data is that workers who are classified as out of the labor force by the BLS, meaning that they do not report having engaged in active search activities in the past four weeks but say they want a job, have virtually the same probability of transitioning to full- time employment as the long-term unemployed.	13	1
201404	3003	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	It’s about half the rate of the short-term unemployed.	13	1
201404	3004	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	That’s true whether they’ve searched in the past year or not, and it’s true whether they say they’re discouraged by economic conditions or not.	13	1
201404	3005	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	This suggests that the traditional distinction between discouraged workers who want a job and workers who aren’t discouraged but say they want a job isn’t as economically meaningful, in my opinion.	13	1
201404	3006	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	Workers who tell the BLS they do not want a job have a markedly lower transition rate, as you’d expect, but, nonetheless, some of them just pop into the labor force.	13	1
201404	3007	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	Holding aside the retirees and the disabled, who have really low transition rates, if you don’t want a job and you’re not in those groups, it’s about one-fourth of the rate of the short-term unemployed.	13	1
201404	3008	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	The relative size of these employment probabilities seems pretty consistent over time, and that motivates what my researchers did, which was to take the weighted sum of the different nonemployed groups.	13	1
201404	3009	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	The weight is the sample average of the employment probability relative to the sample average employment probability of the short-term unemployed.	13	1
201404	3010	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	So the short-term unemployed get a weight of 1, and everyone else gets weights of less than 1.	13	1
201404	3011	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	As you’d expect, the resulting index behaves very much like the unemployment rate, rising in recessions and falling in expansions.	13	1
201404	3012	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	But it’s somewhat smoother and more persistent than the unemployment rate.	13	1
201404	3013	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	The unemployment rate has fallen more rapidly than the nonemployment index since 2009.	13	1
201404	3014	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	It turns out, though, that that always happens in recoveries.	13	1
201404	3015	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	And it turns out that both rates of decline seem consistent with the past recoveries for which we have data.	13	1
201404	3016	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	Plus, if you line up the level of any one nonemployment index—they have four or five versions—it’s about where it was when the unemployment rate last got to where it is now, if you understand what I’m saying.	13	1
201404	3017	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	So in the previous expansion, when did the unemployment rate get to where it is now?	13	1
201404	3018	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	Well, the nonemployment index is about where it was then.	13	1
201404	3019	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	Relative to the unemployment rate, these nonemployment indexes are at about the same level as they were in past expansions.	13	1
201404	3020	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	They even have a version that takes into account part-time employment, although there are some nuances there that they’re still wrestling with.	13	1
201404	3021	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	So, yes, there’s substantial underutilization in the labor market, beyond what is captured in the standard unemployment rate, but, at least according to these measures, no more than is usually associated with this level of unemployment.	13	1
201404	3022	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Can I ask a question?	13	1
201404	3023	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	How does this weigh into the short-term versus long-term unemployment rate distinction?	13	1
201404	3024	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	You seem to be saying that the unemployment rate is a pretty good summary statistic.	13	1
201404	3025	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	So, by inference, you’d then be saying that this distinction between short-term and long-term unemployed doesn’t have a lot of value.	13	1
201404	3026	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	No—it does.	13	1
201404	3027	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Well, it does, but adjusting for that—	13	1
201404	3028	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	But, in terms of employment probability, being in the labor force and long-term unemployed, you look exactly like a discouraged worker.	13	1
201404	3029	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m asking a slightly different question.	13	1
201404	3030	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	You’re basically saying that the unemployment rate today is a good summary measure of unemployment.	13	1
201404	3031	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	Some people are arguing that the unemployment rate today is not a good summary statistic, and that you want to look at the short-term unemployment rate.	13	1
201404	3032	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	Oh, that?	13	1
201404	3033	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	Ah—gee, I don’t know what it says about that.	13	1
201404	3034	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	That’s a good question.	13	1
201404	3035	2014-04-30	meeting	DUDLEY	But you are saying this—that the unemployment rate is a good summary statistic based on that work?	13	1
201404	3036	2014-04-30	meeting	LACKER	Yes.	13	1

201404	3247	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201404	3248	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’ll discuss my national economic outlook, I’ll talk about some information from the Ninth District, and I’ll talk about some interesting econometric analysis my staff has done using cross-MSA data.	13	1
201404	3249	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	My national economic outlook has changed little since the last meeting.	13	1
201404	3250	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The critical feature of that outlook is that, under the assumptions about monetary policy in the Tealbook, Book A, I see inflation running below target until 2018.	13	1
201404	3251	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The situation in the Ninth District supports that low-inflation outlook.	13	1
201404	3252	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As we talked to local contacts, we spent a considerable amount of time trying to elicit information about wage pressures.	13	1
201404	3253	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The unemployment rate is extremely low in parts of the Ninth District.	13	1
201404	3254	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In the Bakken oil counties of eastern Montana and western North Dakota, the unemployment rate is 1.5 percent.	13	1
201404	3255	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In Sioux Falls, South Dakota, the unemployment rate in late 2013 slipped below 3 percent.	13	1
201404	3256	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It should not be surprising that there are signs of noticeable wage pressures in these parts of the District, and there are.	13	1
201404	3257	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But, populationwise, these are small pockets.	13	1
201404	3258	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	More generally in the District, even though the unemployment rate has fallen to under 5 percent, wage pressures remain subdued.	13	1
201404	3259	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Our contacts typically report that current anticipated wage increases lie in the usual tight band between 2 percent and 3 percent.	13	1
201404	3260	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Actually, the conversation that we had yesterday about nominal wage rigidities being responsible for the slow wage growth—President Williams’s remarks yesterday about this—we heard echoed in conversations with our labor contacts earlier this year.	13	1
201404	3261	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	They actually came up with this themselves—nothing prompted it.	13	1
201404	3262	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Employers weren’t able to lower wages enough during the downturn, so they’re waiting before increasing wages on the way out.	13	1
201404	3263	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As I’ve mentioned before, one possible reason why wage pressures have remained subdued is that, although the unemployment rate is close to historical norms in the District, a large fraction of the labor force is working part time for economic reasons.	13	1
201404	3264	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So, even though the unemployment rate has fallen below 5 percent, the fraction of the labor force that’s working part time for economic reasons remains quite high by historical standards.	13	1
201404	3265	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Recently, my staff conducted some empirical work that validated the importance of this metric in assessing inflationary pressures.	13	1
201404	3266	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As you may recall, a few meetings ago, I described the results of cross-MSA, Phillips-curve estimates obtained by Minneapolis Fed staff.	13	1
201404	3267	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	At that time, they had found a stable and plausible relationship between U-3 and inflation.	13	1
201404	3268	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The more recent work has added an additional variable—the fraction of workers who are part time for economic reasons.	13	1
201404	3269	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This variable entered significantly, in both an economic and statistical sense, when they included it in a Phillips-curve regression with the usual unemployment rate, U-3.	13	1
201404	3270	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think it would be interesting, in terms of President Lacker’s description of the work that’s being done by Richmond Fed staff, to try to do the same kind of analysis with their new measure of labor market underutilization and determine how well that predicts inflation across MSAs.	13	1
201404	3271	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, I should emphasize the following point: I see these cross-MSA estimates as being more informative about the true relationship between national unemployment and national inflation than aggregate Phillips curve estimates.	13	1
201404	3272	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Why do I say that?	13	1
201404	3273	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Aggregate Phillips-curve estimates are contaminated by the endogenous response of monetary policy to demand shocks.	13	1
201404	3274	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The cross-MSA results are not contaminated by this response.	13	1
201404	3275	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	You have a local demand shock in Minneapolis–St Paul.	13	1
201404	3276	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The FOMC does not respond to that.	13	1
201404	3277	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Aggregate monetary policy is not responding to MSA-specific shocks.	13	1
201404	3278	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So the cross-MSA estimates are actually cleaner estimates of the aggregate Phillips curve than we can get from aggregate data.	13	1
201404	3279	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	To sum up, like the Tealbook, I continue to expect PCE inflation to remain below target for the next four years.	13	1
201404	3280	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In the Ninth District, wage pressures remain subdued in the face of less than 5 percent unemployment, and Minneapolis Fed empirical work suggests that the high fraction of workers who are part time for economic reasons at the national level will continue to put downward pressure on inflation as the economy improves.	13	1
201404	3281	2014-04-30	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201404	3282	2014-04-30	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1
